when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些 , 但真正的是說未來會比這個多很多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 再次發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論性的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但turing告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論如何做電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你的電腦是否有機械 , 像是babbage的原本 , 或是電子 , 像是電腦今天 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或是細胞 , 還是 , 同樣的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 , 再一次地 , 機械化 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它很小 。 這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂巡迴論點 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到這個連結 , 你說babbage真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們今天用電腦所做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 卡片被餵進去 , 它的跑步速度大約是第一台zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆派克 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以在很多額外的記憶中加入 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有些計劃
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在斯丁文 , 科學博物館檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫的這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個是我們稱之為 「 計劃28 」 的計畫 , 這也是我以doronswaade為起始的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算員 , 也是主導計劃要建造一個差異引擎的人 , 我們的計劃是要建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們將建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案計畫有好幾部分要做 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二個是研究這些計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦如何運作 , 因為與其在你面前有一小片晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我聞起來很可能是它在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	巴貝奇自己寫道 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來的科學課程 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從未打造它 , 因為他總是在做新的計畫 , 但當它的確在1940年代被建造出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓你們稍微了解一下它的樣子 , 用一個影片來說明cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它會補充 。 這是加法動作的機制 , 所以你想像這台巨型機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年的時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們將擁有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像充斥的演講中 , 雅納•亞伯特蘭在他的網路上展示了他三個最近期的計畫 , 關於人性和棲息地 , 在他的系列中驚人的空照片 , 「 來自上方的地球 」 , 來自全球的個人訪談 , 內容是來自他的網路 「 六十億人 」 , 他的索馬利亞電影《家 」 , 記錄了人類對環境的影響 , 透過拍攝影片來對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yanarthusbertrand在廣角捕捉了脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 藉由飛機來到這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸的二氧化碳 , 也就是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡要談生態學 , 一年內 , 我排放的二氧化碳和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我必須殺死一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳抵銷 , 就像我每次都一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我將展示一些我過去一年所拍攝的最後照片的例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的沙油 , 很多污染
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們知道的 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省人民工作非營利組織 , 24小時到7小時 , 盡可能地提取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們對石油的終結
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用石油的三倍之多
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加里多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	2050年以前可能有100%的珊瑚因為全球暖化而滅絕 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	而且你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極 。 去年夏天我已經拍了這張照片 。
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前這張照片是不可能做到的
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	大西洋和太平洋之間有一種新的開拓方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年起就減少了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	有一張沒有冰的吉利曼賈羅的新面孔 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	失去了它80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家的說法 , 在一百年內 , 所有的山冰川都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾告訴各位 , 有二十億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。
return of fish men .	回來的魚男人
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	人類的五分之一依賴魚的生存 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今有70%的魚股被過度利用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據fao , 如果我們不改變我們在2050年捕魚主要的海域資源的系統 , 將會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的

one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物 。

here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國這裡 , 百分之九十的玉米培養是用來餵食動物或做石油的 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	婆羅洲的棕櫚樹種植園

now i am going to speak to you about my movie .	現在我要跟各位談談我的電影 。

the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	電影的名字是 「 家 」 梅森 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:這個地球已經有四十五億年歷史了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年的歷史
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類直立行走只有20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們已經成功地適應了 , 而且已經征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育孩子 , 不像數百萬其他物種住在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我一直很密切地看著地球和它的居住者 , 來自天空的高空 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命和我們星球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕撈、繁殖、耕作 , 仍然是世界上最主要的人類佔有率 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	把我們結合在一起 , 遠大於我們分裂的原因 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的天賦有同樣的需求──同樣的願望──升到我們自己之上 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻帶著提高牆壁 , 以保持我們分離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是保護地球的自然提供 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經更徹底地改變了它 , 而不是整個人類的歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運行率很低
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的農耕正在耗盡土壤
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不可持續 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只想改善生活
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距正在增長 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們的速度比地球能維持的速度更快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道現今的解決方案是可行的 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 讓它變得更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	那我們還在等什麼呢 ?

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克展現出快速基因組定序是多麼的便宜和快感 , 將健康照護顛覆 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、健康照護、科學、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我向你們介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男人有x , 當然 , 還有y的小副本 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是一個微小的小東西讓你變得不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的代碼--這四個生化字母--或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 對 , 是a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是個大數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280個像素上的每個像素放到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順帶一提 , y染色體決定要將它定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以15年後 , 事實上 , 大約40億美元之後 , 基因組定序並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被發表了 , 他們繼續著手進行 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一個看起來像這樣的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基層的成本大約是一美元--一個非常緩慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們採取一個基因組 , 我們製造了大約50本 , 把所有的複本都切割成小五十個元 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行進行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	接著 , 我們將它帶入軟體中 , 我們把它重新組合起來 , 告訴你故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓大家看一下這是什麼樣子 , 人類基因組計畫:3gb , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台在其中一台機器上運行:一週有200gbas 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天將有200個變化到600個 , 沒有這種速度減慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 基地的價格 , 為了定序一個基地 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等同於你在1998年把車子裝滿氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星 , 再開兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc定位、所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、舊有的定序方式 , 這裡有所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是木頭尺碼 ; 你通常不會看到像這樣一直上升的線 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 全世界人類基因組測序的能力大約是今年的5萬到10萬組人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們依據被放置的機器知道這點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期在可預見的未來中一年會有兩倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室 , 代表所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做 「 北京基因組研究所 」 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國人絕對要贏得這場比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼呢 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人37歲
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她會出現 「 階段2 」 雌激素受體乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又回到了 「 階段三 」 卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲回來 , 患有更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性骨髓性白血病回來
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人接受治療的方式 , 短短的十年內 , 看起來會像血管一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所的人們決定要看一看這位女士後遺症
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	然後他定序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 還有癌症的骨髓 , 他在幾週內完成了整個基因組的排序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他將這兩組基因組做比較 , 他在軟體中發現 , 在其它東西當中 , 是一個刪除 , 一個2000個核元的刪除 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 跨越30億個鹼基的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種惡性突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女子沒有幫助 , 但它的確有很嚴重、很深刻的影響 , 如果你願意的話 , 對她的家庭有影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 且他們得到了這個基因測試 , 然後他們了解它 , 那他們就可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 他們可以早期抓到癌症 , 很有可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀並不符合 , 透過一些英雄的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的是雙向肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了貓頭鷹 , 他們的症狀確實有所改善 , 但他們並沒有完全的不友善 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	原來這張照片裡的先生是一位叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家名為生命科技的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是這兩家公司製造大量基因組定序工具的其中一家 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 在一個叫做spr的基因中有一系列的突變 , 負責產生血清素 , 和其他東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在絕對食品藥物管理局的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素的先驅藥品 , 現在有效地正常了 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 若沒有完整的基因定序就不會發生這種事 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在當時--這是幾年前--花費十萬美金
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美金 , 明年是一千美金
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在它100美元後的那一年 , 給予或花一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這動作有多快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小nick喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 肚子像個飢荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	不是說他不吃飯 , 而是當他吃飯時 , 他的腸道基本上打開了 , 糞便溢出到他的腸道中 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百個手術之後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請禱告我 , 我在這麼多的痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因組排序吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 在一個控制細胞死亡的基因中單一點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是他對食物本質上發生的一些免疫反應 , 這是自然反應 , 造成一些程式化細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但調節下來的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也是一種治療骨髓移植手術的方法 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的辛苦康復後 , 他現在用a1醬來吃牛排 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身上 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 這意味著在座的每個人都可以多活個5、10、20年 , 只因為這個東西 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你考慮人類在地球上的足跡 , 以及我們保持食物生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植玉米、小麥、大豆和其他作物 , 都非常包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得要繼續成長 , 吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要採取的位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有人願意自願停止吃東西 ?

this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來每台桌上型電腦的釘子 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraftdemos--他的骨髓礦物--一個新裝置 , 很快地將生命的骨髓存放到捐贈者身上 。 他強調成人幹細胞在骨髓裡可以被用來治療許多臨終條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	現在 , jillboltetaylor去年的靈感來源 , 我並沒有帶人腦來 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的性命 , 大部分的人都擁有先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國 , 拯救一個有白血病孩子的性命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何採收這種骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉、護士 , 和我的另一位醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob在桌上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們的做法是 , 把這個放在軟組織中 , 然後把它打進硬骨 , 進入tuchus這個術語 , 每次用針筒取出十mls的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將它切成一個錫 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交回給我 。 我們一而再、再而三地重複這件事 。
about 200 times usually .	通常大約有200次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在結束前 , 我的手臂是如此 , 我手上有一個叫聲 , 更不用說bob , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 就像瑞士起司一樣 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道嗎 , 這個程序已經40年沒有改變了 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個最微不足道的入侵方式 , 一個我們稱為 「 骨髓採礦者 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採取器 , 它的運作方式在這裡顯示
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準來看病患 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭幾十次 , 我們只會進入到臀部的前面或臀部的後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個有彈性、有力的導管 , 有一個特別的電線尖 , 會留在骨髓的殘酷部位 , 跟著臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常快速地嚮往 , 或吸出豐富的骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以在同一個入口處多次通過 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob可以用一種穿刺的方式 , 局部麻醉 , 將它當作一種向外收穫 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 , 拿到史丹佛的小額貸款
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到兩隻大型動物 , 豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們驚訝地發現 , 我們不僅僅拿出骨髓 , 還拿到骨髓中的幹細胞活動 , 從骨髓礦物中得到十倍 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在過去一年才剛核准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一位活體病患 。 你可以看到它跟著周圍的彈性曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡將會有兩個在同一個病人 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉劑下進行的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的 , 我們得到的幹細胞比同一個病人的標準方法還要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞非常豐富的來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們全身 , 包括我們骨髓裡的血液循環性幹細胞 , 我們用這種形式的幹細胞 , 做為幹細胞治療已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年中 , 使用骨髓幹細胞的爆炸 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 例如心臟病、血管疾病、整形病、組織工程、甚至神經學 , 來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 正在商業化 , 今年 , 2.0個骨髓礦工的世代 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多的幹細胞 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為有潛在救命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能讓你在年輕更健康時 , 銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 用在未來應該需要它的時候 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這張照片是我們骨髓移植者的骨髓移植者 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi在宇宙中展示了一個有爭議的新模型 , 也許只是回答了所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他問題 , 它是最美麗的八維模型 , 基本粒子和力 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	他對萬物理論的garretlisi
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我會盡我所能地描述粒子物理學的美麗 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗又不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚頭都包含數以千計的珊瑚 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚苯二甲酸酯會不斷地分裂成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個超級智慧的珊瑚 , 我們就可以一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 他在這特定的地點 , 與鄰居相比 , 如果這只是機會 , 或命運 , 又是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在把溫度調高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以是相當的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤 , 可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這可能性會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居對他的複本很明顯是一模一樣的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也身處在其他地方 , 身為獨立的個體 ,
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超智能的珊瑚會特別準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是很奇怪的一件事 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪最初是用艾文薛丁格和他的貓來形容的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設備中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的箱子中 , 通過量子力學定律 , 分支到一個放射性及狀態中 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	樣本放射線的分支中 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁格就死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的其他分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些真實是每個個體的獨立體驗 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	無論如何 , 另一個都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這似乎對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只會經歷一個個別存在 , 而我們卻無法看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 如薛丁格在這裡 , 是一種珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 這是世界在微小規模的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一個句子來總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理是關於描述可能發生的事和無法發生的事 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們 , 一切都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的相互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麼以及它們的平衡如何運作 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 質子和反質子的光束會加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在撞擊中結合 , 產生出一股純粹的能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 和偵測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--日內瓦的大型強子對撞機有17英里的圓環 , 當它在運作時 , 能畫出蒙特雷市的五倍電力 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們粒子可以產生什麼
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量都必須和質子和質子一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這能量限制更質量的粒子都不會產生 , 而對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新粒子加速器如此興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量極限推到前所未有的七倍以上 , 所以我們很快就會看到一些新粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在場的很多人都把他們推來推去 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中性伴侶叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和一個非常小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下夸克有非常大的質量 , 三者結合起來 , 讓原子內的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都來到左手邊和右手邊的品種 , 都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也有較少的第二代和第三代相同的載荷但質量較高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都與各式各樣的力子相互作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電荷相互作用 , 通過光子所謂的粒子 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力量 , 叫做 「 不可想像力 」 , 弱力只會和左撇子相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 叫做顏色載荷 , 帶有三種不同品種:紅色、綠色和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann這些名字--他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉與物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	這裡要了解的最重要的是 , 每一種力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的相應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還未被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給予了所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子我們幾乎可以確定它會
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們可能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	接下來我要給你們看一個美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演講的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多粒子可以持續追蹤的 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	自然界中有這麼多基本粒子似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控畫出它們 , 有些美麗的圖案就會浮現出來 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷 , 夸克則有電荷三分之一 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合來製造一個質子時 , 它有一個總電荷加上一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也具有反粒子 , 具有反電荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩種載荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們散播出超荷和弱荷 , 並在這個二維載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷 , 電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力相互作用 , 根據它們的超荷和弱荷 , 產生這種模式 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 統一的電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被拼湊起來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩種都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量 , 打破了這個電波圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	藉由給弱粒子一個大的質量使弱力變得非常微弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於這個大規模的希格斯粒子沿著這個平面方向坐著 , 電磁學的光子維持無質量 , 並且沿著電荷方向進行電荷互動 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力是用這種在二維空間中的粒子載荷的模式所描述的
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力包含在兩種載荷的方向 , 沿著夸克粒子的載荷畫出來 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷都可以在四維載荷空間中畫出來 , 向下投射到二維空間 , 這樣我們就可以看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然就會把東西保持在完美的平衡 , 沿著四個載荷方向前進 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子碰撞 , 它就會產生能量和總載荷 , 四個載荷方向都有零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以被創造出來只要它有相同能量並保持完全零載荷
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這個弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在撞擊中被創造出來 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在更進一步的互動中 , 指控總是保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱子可能衰退成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個仍然是零電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些載荷的模式不只美麗 ,
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼互動是被允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 讓它更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這個很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強力相互作用中 , 一個強力粒子 , 例如這個 , 會和彩色夸克相互作用 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 給一個夸克有不同的顏色載荷這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強相互作用每秒發生幾百萬次發生在我們體內的每一個原子裡 , 把原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷相對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再包含兩種載荷來對應重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	包括這些 , 每個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都會分裂 , 並在六維載荷空間中給予一個不錯的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看到它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前對於大自然如何在這些基本粒子的微小規模之下建立的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗能達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小尺度的運作方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的新點子 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想用數學來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們是否能在整個enchilada手上拿到 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想找尋我們宇宙中所有能做出完整圖像的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子我們會看到何時實驗達到更高的能量
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以粒子物理學有一個舊觀念就是這種已知的載荷模式 , 這種不太對稱的模式 , 可能從一個更完美的圖案中浮現出來 , 會變得像希格斯粒子一樣 , 如何打破電力發射模式 , 來給電磁力學 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向來引進新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引入一個新方向時 , 我們得先猜測 , 粒子的載荷是什麼 , 沿著這個方向進行轉動 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六個載荷維度中建構標準載荷 , 作為這七個載荷維度中更為完美的對稱 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇與1973年由pati和salam推出的一個大統一理論相對應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到有幾個缺口 , 粒子似乎缺少了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的工作方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 包含了被建立的模式作為子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該要作用的很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這一組載荷 , 並考慮一個關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中 , 物質的第二代和第一代擁有完全一樣的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非獨一無二地被它們的六個載荷給辨識出來 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們在標準載荷空間中互相坐在對方的位置 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那我們就可以分配每個粒子的獨特新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二和第三代的物質與第一代的對稱是 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度空間中這個特別的載荷模式其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外謊言組 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑、曲線的形狀有248維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每一點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中的曲線時間 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	和量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙如何在最小的尺度下運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這個形狀存在於八維載荷空間的圖案很精緻地美麗 , 它總結出了數千種可能的相互作用 , 在這些基本粒子之間 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個面向 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	用一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以沿著一個對稱軸看下去八度空間 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們都能看到新粒子所需要的一些洞 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個空隙 , 新粒子應該是哪裡有2個空隙 , 其中兩個已經被派塔斯拉姆粒子給填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們在這個圖案中的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該像希格斯粒子一樣 , 但有顏色充電 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個圖案 , 讓我們得到完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有非常深的數學根 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美的物體能以最小尺度描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這種自然界被數學所描述的理念 , 並不是全新的想法 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的大本書 , 它持續地開放我們的眼睛 , 用數學的語言寫著 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有它 , 它是人類無法理解它的單一個字 ; 沒有這些 , 一個人就在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形來描述粒子物理學的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我其實在研究這個東西時 , 數學可以和黑暗迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但讓人放心的是 , 在這個數學的核心是純粹的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個地點相互作用 , 根據美麗的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的模式出現 , 使用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們或許可以看出大自然是否使用這e8圖案或另一種 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這種發現的過程是一場美好的冒險 , 能夠參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合e8圖案的粒子那會非常、非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟糕呢 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作 , 是個很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這種理論和其他類似的理論是漫長的 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人很努力地知道 , 這些想法大部分可能最後都不會成為自然界的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多的野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資一樣 , 在不出手時 , 要放棄一系列研究是很困難的 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果某樣東西沒用 , 你就得把它丟掉 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 維持理智和達成這不確定性的唯一方法就是在生活中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經竭盡所能過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪之間平衡我的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我所研究的物理學一無是處 , 我仍然知道我過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去10年來我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在是宇宙中最偉大的奧秘之一 , 讓我爸媽知道我如何在沒有全職工作的情況下 , 活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我把這個秘密給你們看 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我的家 , 在毛伊島辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租讓我花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧的存在有時是很艱難的 , 但它讓我可以住在美麗的地方 , 保持我人生中的平衡 , 讓我很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間在超智能珊瑚身上 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能在這裡受邀來ted演講 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 它之所以有少數人至少很興奮 , 是因為 , 如果你說對了 , 它會把引力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該把宇宙想成是宇宙中最小的東西 , 不知何故是e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 還是...
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	波特:嗯 , 我展示給各位看的圖案 , 相對於我們所知的基本粒子物理學 , 已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那就是我們肯定知道的那個 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀和e8圖案的相似度有驚人的相似之處 , 可能就是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看過的這些點圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它會在空間時間上扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就是我們看到的這些基本粒子的解釋 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論家 , 如我所理解的 , 解釋了電子 , 以更小的弦震動來說 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們應該如何看待一個電子在和e8的關係中 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	波特:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它是扭動的 。 當它移動時 , 它的方向是扭動的 。 我們看到的是什麼粒子 。 克:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子的關係如何 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	為了我的照片 , 我覺得我需要這樣做 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	波特:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小的可能性 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有可能性都同時擴大和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我用珊瑚的類比
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的出現方式就是在時空中每一處附著的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀的扭曲方向的扭曲形狀在這個曲線的表面上扭曲是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 它們將自己表達成點 , 並以這種方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再說清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它喚起了一種奇妙的感覺 , 我當然也想了解更多這種感覺 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來到這裡 , 這真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍•古德會談到塔可爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助在非洲的小鎮增長 , 居住在有威脅性的動物旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德能幫助人類和動物生活在一起 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 賈莫 , 安布蘭 , 邦西爾 , 但我們也可以去 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群蟻巢傳到下一群 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上我想從zeray昨天離開的地方拿起我的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個驚人、三歲的南方古猿孩童 , selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也常聽到透過dna側寫 , 人類的族譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	這是一位古生物學家 , 已故路易斯.勒克 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時還蠻不尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在有點常見 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石、肌肉附著物的形狀來分辨這些人長什麼樣子 , 和他們從各式各樣的手工藝品一起生活 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但它們的行為如何呢 ? 這就是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張 , 現在是個相當普遍的理論 , 如果我們在最接近的居住親戚身上發現了類似的行為模式 , 和現在的人類一樣 , 那麼也許那些行為出現在人猿身上 , 七百萬年前的人類祖先 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們將這些特徵從古老的過去帶給我們 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你去看現今處理人類進化的教科書 , 你常常會發現人們在推測早期人類的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們和我們一樣 , 比起任何其他生物 , 我們在ted大會上都聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以這對我來說還是要評論黑猩猩在某些方面和我們很像 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外生存到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲爾先生 。 雌猩猩在11或12歲時 , 生了她的第一個寶寶 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她只有一個嬰兒 , 每五、六年 , 在孩童護理時 , 長時間的孩童依賴性 , 晚上和母親同睡 , 背上騎著 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信 , 這種長期的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像我們在學習時期一樣 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更加複雜 , 以不同形式的動物演化 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在一個人的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間看他們的長輩做了什麼 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 以這種方式來看 , 現今在所有不同黑猩猩族群中所看到的不同的工具行為 , 如何從一個世代傳播到下一個世代 , 透過觀察、模仿和實踐 , 這樣我們才能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們也談過
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的姿勢和姿勢非常豐富 , 其中許多都很相似 , 甚至相同 , 以相同的形式 , 形成在相同的情境中 。 迎接黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻 , 手牽手 , 背上向對方拍手 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後牠們游動然後丟石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多許多同情心的例子 , 前往愛情和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有著黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極端殘酷 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具攻擊性的行為 , 大部分的部分 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常具侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	比起其他生物 , 我相信黑猩猩 , 比起任何其他生物 , 都能幫助我們了解 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物界之間並沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們更加觀察 , 越來越模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外的複雜的社會生活中 , 幫助了我們認識到我們是其中的一員 , 卻不分開 , 和我們共享地球的動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很讓人難過的發現 , 像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它向你展示了岡貝的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	大約16年前我飛越整個區域 , 意識到在公園之外 , 這片森林 , 在1960年的森林中 , 幾乎毫無疑問地沿著坦尚尼加湖的東岸延伸 , 這片小小的 , 30平方公園出現了 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的人們在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地能支撐更多人 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民數量的增加 , 是因為從蒲隆地倒進來的難民數量 , 來自剛果的湖泊 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個程式 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常全面的方式來改善居住在公園附近村莊的人的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	由12個村莊開始 , 現在已經24歲了
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入研究 , 包括樹木護理 , 農耕方式最適合這種方式 , 現在已經非常惡化 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的土地 , 在這些山中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤侵蝕的方法
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新找回過度使用的農地 , 這樣在兩年內 , 他們就可以再次生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力幫助村民從井裡取得新鮮水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和小群婦女合作 , 提供小額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	我們得到的 , 如同全世界的情況 , 大約有95%的貸款返回 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性能力 , 和教育一起工作 , 為女孩提供獎學金 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 明確地了解到 , 在全世界 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模的改善 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供關於家庭計畫和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 保育有一些事情正在發生 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的現況是 , 住在這24個村莊的農夫 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一大群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始塔科爾計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞隊伍進入了村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞隊伍和村民對話 , 問問他們有興趣什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康很有興趣 ; 他們對教育很有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間持續下去 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始對保育的需求有更多的了解 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山丘的上層層被樹木給摧毀 , 所以你有這片可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥土 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發所謂的更偉大的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園以外的地區 , 延伸到非常退化的土地中 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實也同意將百分之十到二十的土地放到高地之外 , 這樣一來 , 當樹木長回來時 , 黑猩猩就會有葉門走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園以外的遺傳可行性交流 。
so tacare is a success .	所以tacare是成功的
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地區複製它 , 圍繞著其他面對極端人口壓力的荒野地區 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們在ted的前幾天所討論的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有非常多的貧窮 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的人住在土地上 , 並不是那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍伐樹木 , 把土壤開放給侵蝕 , 隨著絕望的族群砍伐了越來越多的樹木 , 這樣他們就能嘗試為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ?
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	不只是非洲的問題 , 還有其他發展中國家的其他問題 , 的確 , 到處都是 , 我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說 , 如果地球上每一個人都能依照歐洲或美國人的平均生活標準來看 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題來了 , 這裡可說是走過地球上最有智慧的生物 , 帶著這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠由這些ted大會所闡釋的科技 , 然而我們卻在破壞我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 習慣四處坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們的人民前七代 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決策──而我不是在這裡特別談論非洲 , 但已開發國家的重大決策──涉及數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響下一次股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲四處旅行 , 談論黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我了解到越來越多非洲問題可以被解決 , 如同之前殖民時代的大門 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲演講 , 在美國演講 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些糟糕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而且你知道我在說的那種 , 我說的污染
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源也許是我們本世紀中所要面對最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都有水被農業、工業和家庭化學物質污染 , 仍然在世界各地噴灑 , 看似沒有從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 海嘯之類的影響會越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們談過土壤侵蝕
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們和其他溫室氣體燃燒化石燃料的魯莽 , 所以 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候發生了一些非常錯誤的事 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混雜在一起
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受影響較嚴重的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	是非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱情況更糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨水來臨時 , 它通常會造成洪水 , 加上苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而生活在土地無法支撐的地區 , 貧窮到無法買食物 , 因為整片土地都被降低了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化感 , 哭泣 , 哭泣 , 哭泣 , 因為最後一棵樹被砍掉了 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種東西不只在非洲 , 遍佈全世界 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個特別聰明的大腦之間可能有某種隔閡嗎 ? ted技術展現出來的那種大腦 , 而人類的心 ? 用非科學的角度來說 , 用愛和同情的角度來說 , 能否有一些隔閡 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們不是很沮喪 , 就是很冷漠 , 或很生氣 。 他們說 , 或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們會這樣感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 我們也沒辦法對它做任何事 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 從我年紀開始 , 我感受到這個絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	後來我們稱這個計畫為根與芽 , 從坦尚尼亞這裡開始 , 現在已經推廣到全世界97個國家了 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	這是象徵性的 , 根製造堅定的基礎
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射線似乎很小 ; 要到達太陽 , 它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為我們在地球上所面臨的所有問題 , 環境和社會的問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人 , 可以突破 , 讓這個世界更美好 , 適合所有生物 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人都做出改變 , 每一天
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有一個選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都有一個選擇 , 可以選擇我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人別無選擇 , 要改變窮人也有選擇
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的團體全都選擇了三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年紀多大 , 而哪個國家 , 不論他們在哪個城市或鄉村 , 都要看哪些計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多成人開始他們自己的根與芽的團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一個團體在他們之間選擇三個不同種類的計畫 , 來讓這個世界變得更好 , 意識到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會籌錢幫助世界其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個計畫是幫助動物不僅是野生動物、家居動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切的過程中 , 提到學習活在我們內在的和平和諧中 , 在我們的家庭中、我們的社區中、國家之間、文化之間、宗教之間 , 和自然世界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然的世界 。 我們不能以我們目前的速度去摧毀它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要在非洲挑選一個或兩個項目 , 即根與芽的團體正在進行 , 一、二個項目只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果、剛果、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我所說 , 這是在全世界97個國家中 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞一起工作 , 以少量的金錢賣蛋 , 或只是用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 並感受到驕傲和賦權 , 因為他們不再無助 , 依賴別人的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理幫助 , 讓士兵來實現 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫 , 是把他們自己帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會上有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間找到更多的根與芽 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也致力於愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 與年長的孩子和較年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不願懷孕之類的 , 年輕人從其他青年中傾聽得更好 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的東西 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數量從一百萬隻 , 到一百五十萬隻 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經有森林的沙漠
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這個了不起的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我非常興奮 , 最後 , 來找人談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	是我其中一個嗜好者
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把這些水沖下梯 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著談到再生能源──絕對重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心地球給我們的孩子 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有孩子或孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的精英 , 我們可以為此做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天的生活做選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼、穿什麼、
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	而選擇用問題來做出這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周圍的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 會如何影響我孩子的生命 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或其它的
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 與人類的心相結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted的幫助 , google也幫助我們 , esri也在gmbe國家公園的地圖上幫我們繪製 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們將它們串聯起來 , 已經開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	各位今天下午已經聽過了 , 開始發生了
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 若要看到我們關心未來 , 我們一定要有的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個理由希望大自然是驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要時間 , 或許就能協助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是塔卡爾計畫 。
