i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴各位 , 看似死樹木的地點 , 如果你停止砍伐火木 , 因為你有很多木材 , 那麼五年內你就可以有一棵三十英尺長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕邊緣 , 可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 它帶我到最後一類的希望 , 在過去的兩天中 , 我們已經聽過這麽多的事:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種對人類精神的堅定性 , 人類精神的堅定性 , 如此一來 , 那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病給打擊的人 , 或其他的 , 都可以把自己從中抽離出來 , 有時只要用手協助 , 把他們在社會中的一部分拿去改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想非洲有一兩個人真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以做一張很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 曼德拉從十七年的辛勤勞力浮現 , 二十三年的監禁 , 帶著寬恕的能力 , 這麼一來 , 他就能帶領他的國家走出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 不用放血澡 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	kensarowiwa , 在奈及利亞 , 他接下了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都盡了全力 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此的鼓舞人心
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們年輕非洲人需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天已經聽過其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感激這個機會能再次分享這個訊息 , 和ted的所有人分享 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起談這些 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一個單詞是這整個會議中心的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她對她的證書感到很興奮 。 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說幫助她做她正在做的事
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常非常興奮 , 能見到她 , 看到年輕人如何被賦予權力的其中一個例子 , 因為有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於海洋和我們生活中的塑膠污染的艱難事實 , 還有一些關於如何解放我們自己如何從塑膠漩渦中解放的思想 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 我把這些塑膠袋剪下來 , 縫合在一起 , 做為我的藝術作品過去二十年來的主要材料 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二和三維的作品 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	在與塑膠共事八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂成小小的塑膠碎片 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	像我們一樣的短暫 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在進一步教育我自己 , 關於塑膠 , 其實我發現這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	這是一件壞事 , 塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它總是塑膠的 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多在海洋環境中
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去的幾年中 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾堆和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我的初步反應和我認為這是很多人對學習的第一反應就是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須到外面去清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我真的開發了一個提案 , 用貨船出海 , 還有兩艘分解的捕魚拖網漁船 , 一台起重機 , 一台盜獵機 , 和一台冷藏機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是要走出去 , 提高對於這個議題的認知 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 把它切成一小塊 , 再冷到磚塊中 , 可能被當作建材 , 在沒有開發的社區中 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些實際去過河流的人談話 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 然後開始做這件事 , 我了解到 , 相對於每天在世界各地生產的桶子 , 我需要回頭看看更大的景象 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切斷單使用和即丟塑膠的噴霧劑 , 每天進入海洋環境 , 以全球性的規模來看 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這點 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠你想想像在太平洋中間我發現現在有11個塑膠垃圾可能是世界上五大洋的塑膠
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不只是那個我關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦也是超市裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都被包裝在塑膠中 , 即使是在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 也很關心從塑膠中和從塑膠滲入我們體內的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起 , 他們都在研究這個議題 , 我們創立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多正在努力的倡議 , 但其中有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的百分之八十到九十是我們在海洋中發現的殘骸是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱它為什麼 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書中都有關於永續經營和綠化的概念 , 關於回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	那其中的現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠不到7%被回收 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你深入研究 , 特別是在塑膠瓶中 , 大部分只能下降 , 或密封 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降低了 , 變成較少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不可能再次成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大議題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在研究並要求人們去思考的事情是 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面加入了第四個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	不論何時可能 , 拒絕單一使用和丟棄塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是非常古老的學者 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的餅乾容器 , 用它們 , 而不是用它們 , 用它們來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我正在為自己和我的家人做一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一個不鏽鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 卻忘了帶你不鏽鋼瓶 , 用水或濾水填充物 , 而不是買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說我知道你們知道很多關於這個議題的事 , 是因為這在海洋中是很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者所造成的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對議題的意識來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時可能 , 要選擇替代方案 , 選擇單向使用塑膠 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些浪潮切到我們的海洋中 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這段影片來自麻省理工學院的pattimaes實驗室 , 由pranavfrotry推出的 , 是ted的buzzz 。 這是個可穿戴式裝置 , 裝上一個投影機 , 以深刻的互動方式鋪路 。 想像一下 , 《少數民族報告》 , 然後一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	demo , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂•馬斯和帕納•密特瑞•狄摩斯和帕納•狄摩斯和帕納•迪斯特雷夫第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直在想我們是否能進化或發展出第六感 , 一種能讓我們無縫接觸及容易取得的新陳代謝或可能存在的資訊 , 這些資訊可能與我們有相關 , 能協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們要面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們當中有些人可能會爭辯說 , 嗯 , 今天的手機不是已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted這裡遇見某人這是最頂尖的網絡地點 , 當然 , 在那一年你不會握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能不能在我拿出手機和谷歌搜尋你一會兒 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超市的時候 , 站在那一大道不同類型的衛生紙上時 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 然後打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著判斷這些不同衛生紙的哪個是最環保的購買工具 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們真的無法輕易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只要能協助我們做出最佳決定 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在開發一系列的發明 , 來讓我們用一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 而不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭示我們最新的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力仍然是過程中的一份工作 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在戴著這個裝置 , 我們已經把這個裝置拼湊起來了 , 上面的零件都脫離了架子 , 順帶一提 , 目前這個時段只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我穿著攝影機 , 只是個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式、電池驅動的投影系統 , 用一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件會在我的口袋裡通訊到我的手機 , 它的功能是通訊和計算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密特里 , 他真的是那個一直在實施和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走向任何表面 , 開始用他的雙手來和前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤了四隻顯著的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記蓋子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以把指甲塗成不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上可以追蹤這四隻手指並辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 這樣他就可以去 , 比如說 , 一張長灘的地圖 , 放大放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍照 」 手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以直接走到任何一面牆上 , 投影所有他拍攝的照片 , 整理這些照片 , 然後重新整理 , 等等 , 再用所有天然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 你們當中一些人最有可能是在兩年前 , 看到傑夫•漢的示範 , 或者有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以取得 , 和這些投影的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 而且可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的差異是它完全是行動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天它的成本不會比今天的手機要來得多 , 實際上 , 包裝看起來不會更大 , 比我脖子上的這個版本還時髦 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但不只讓你們其中一些人活在幻想中 , 在《少數族群報告》中 , 湯姆•克魯斯很酷的幻想 , 我們對於這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它真的可以作為這第六感的裝置之一 , 讓你能有相關的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超市 , 他正在買紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起產品時 , 系統可以辨識出他拿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識器或標記技術 , 給他綠光或橙色光 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	這個選擇特別好 , 因為他個人的標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能希望衛生紙有最多的白色 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿amazon評分 , 會被投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜的評價很棒 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , pranav翻了這本書的頁面 , 然後就可以看出書本讀者評論的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家的評論 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面上 , 他可能會找到我們朋友的註解 , 給他一點點額外的資訊 , 關於該頁的資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙--它從來不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解--你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是個更具爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你和ted的某人互動時 , 也許你可以看到標籤中的一個字雲 , 和那個人在部落格和個人網頁上的字詞連結在一起 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對相機很感興趣 , 諸如此類 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機經過 , 它可以告訴你你的飛行遲緩了 , 登機門也改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道當下的時光是什麼 , 就跟在手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在發展第六感的地方 , 讓我們能無縫接觸所有相關資訊 , 關於我們可能碰到的資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確值得鼓掌 , 因為我覺得他在過去三個月內睡得不多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他感到不滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但這還不是完美的 , 它是進步中的一項工作 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許在接下來的10年內 , 我們將帶著終極第六感的大腦植入到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	2001年9月11日 , 費利斯•羅德里格茲和艾卡斯•艾薩瓦菲有個強大的友誼 , 由於無法想像的損失而死 。 羅德里格茲的兒子在世貿中心攻擊中被殺害 。 艾爾瓦菲的兒子扎瑟•莫薩索伊被定罪 , 在那些攻擊中扮演了一個角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽得要開始了解並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11癒合:那些發現寬恕、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲利斯•羅德里格茲:今天我們來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為很不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說感覺很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次得知我兒子曾在2001年9月11日的世貿中心
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在36小時後就死了 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將要做什麼 , 以我們兒子的名義──我的丈夫、奧蘭多、我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	而當我看到--然而 , 透過震驚 , 可怕的震撼 , 以及我們生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六個陰謀犯下恐怖主義時 , 美國政府向他索取死刑 , 如果被定罪 , 我和我先生在公開反對這一點時 , 公開對此表示反對 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那樣和透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家庭聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 當她的兒子被指示出來時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人啊 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我更強壯的時候想見那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲慟中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們學到她的兒子被指控的事時 , 她並沒有得到同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月見面 , 艾卡現在會告訴你這是怎麼回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我與受害者的父母聯絡 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	然後我看到phyllis , 我看著她 ,
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的媽媽 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人則是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為媽媽時常受苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我14歲的時候結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 一個十六歲時的第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	zacarias的故事實在太多了
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然痛苦 , 因為我的兒子就像他活著 ,
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否遭受折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 讓我的痛苦對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有婦女來說 , 所有能給予生命的媽媽 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定是手牽手一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 為了我們女人 , 為了我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 對抗恐怖主義 。

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們坐在一個圈子中 , 帶著支持、協助 , 從人們經歷過這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對於你們家庭發生的事有多麼抱歉 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 我覺得如果有罪 , 一個人應該被公平地審判和懲罰 。 」

and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	當時的情況是 , 我們都說了我們的故事 , 我們都以人為本 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在下午結束的時候 , 大約是午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像我們永遠認識彼此一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不只可以在這些當下的情況下這麼慷慨 , 還有當時的狀況 , 還有她兒子身上的一切 , 還有她所擁有的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過有這麼艱苦人生的人 , 從我自己的文化和環境中 ,
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一個特別的連結 , 我非常重視這個連結 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這就是要害怕對方 , 但要踏出那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼困難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能碰到誰呢 ? 我不知道 , 還是我和誰這麼不一樣 ? 」

because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。

by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順帶一提 , 自從我開始演講之後 , 世界上還有一萬三千人正在腹瀉受苦 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節坐下來的那天 , 當時我在看亞洲海嘯爆發的毀滅性新聞 , 在電視上播放 。

okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在對科學研究
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifessaver之前 , 最好的手推過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	所以那肯定會穿越那200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	生命安全氣孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有任何東西能穿透 。

now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我流下水 , 無菌的飲用水就會跑出來 。

traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?

and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫進入營地以取得安全的飲用水 。

diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病擴散 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變成自我發展 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思維 , 運送這些 , 人們可以保持放置 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌的飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎建設和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你在計算器上運行數字時 , 你就跑了出去 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這是 「 思考 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 和使用人造過程來完成它 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個絕佳的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費地把它運送到那邊 , 然後把它倒到山上、河流上 , 和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	而人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源 。

the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的科技 , 在一個jerry罐頭裡
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理兩萬五千公升的水 ; 這對一個四、三年的家庭來說是好的 。
and how much does it cost ?	而要花多少錢呢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大概要半分錢才能跑 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 透過不同的思考 , 並在使用時處理水源 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天走四個小時來收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的源頭取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓人們無法取得安全的飲用水 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要將此情境化為情境 , 英國政府每年花大約120億英鎊在外援上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼就這樣停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	因此每年有三十五億人受苦 , 而每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 將會活著 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown主張我們生活在歷史上一個時刻 , 權力在改變前所未有的方式 。 在tedxbrussels的演講中 , 他列出了前所未有的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashdown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩是十九世紀末非常著名的英文詩人所寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代在邱吉爾的腦中迴盪
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	詩的內容是: 「 夏天的雪山上 , 懶惰地流著 , 哈雷克我聽到遠端鼓聲 , 在夢中打鼓 , 遠、低、低、低音 , 在地球的道路上打鼓 , 靠著朋友、食物到粉末、士兵遊行 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " shroprerelad " 由a.e.豪斯曼所寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所了解的 , 在尼爾森交響曲中也聽到了 , 那就是十九世紀的漫長、熱、銀色的夏天正要來臨 , 我們即將要邁入史上最可怕的一段時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著動盪 , 通常是血 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是:我相信我們被譴責了 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上那些時刻的其中一個時刻 , 當權力被建立起來時 , 權力開始有所改變 , 新世界的外觀、新世界的新力量 , 已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到 , 幾乎總是非常動盪的時刻 , 高度困難的時代 , 以及所有太常血腥的時刻 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 大約每個世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會認為 , 上次發生了──也就是豪斯曼的感覺──以及邱吉爾的感受──也就是 , 當權力從舊的國家傳過去 , 歐洲的舊勢力──橫跨大西洋 , 橫跨美國的新興大西洋──美國的新興勢力──美國本世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在過去曾有過歐洲權力的真空狀態下 , 在上個世紀 , 兩場血腥的災難中 , 第一部分和第二部分:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是一種更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在一個這樣的時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我想談談現今的三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一種 , 前兩種 , 是有關權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於我想要參考的新維度 , 在現在的情況中從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力的轉變 , 正發生在這個世界中 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 非常嚇人 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了日後的權力轉移──希臘的權力──傳到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力轉移──但我們看到了一些稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	對於權力 , 不僅是從國與國之間的移動 ,
it's also moving vertically .	也會垂直地移動
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今的情況是 , 被放置的權力 , 持有責任 , 保持法律的統治 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 現在已經遷移到非常大的全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談到全球化的市場 , 但實際上卻是真正的權力全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級上 , 權力是負責任的主體 , 在法治的階段 , 不在國際階段 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台的權力:網際網路的權力、衛星廣播的權力、金錢改變者的權力──這廣大的貨幣轉換者──現在流通的金錢佔了交易所必要的金額的32倍──它應該是金錢轉換者所在的金融推銷者 , 如果你喜歡的話 , 金融推銷者最近已經把我們所有人帶到我們的膝蓋的權力 , 現在的多國企業現在發展的預算大於中等國家 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些居住在全球的空間 , 很大程度上是不受規範的 , 不受法律規範的影響 , 人們也可能採取不受限制的行動 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這套裝備能提升到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些在沒有限制的空間中運作最有權力的人 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 不久後 , 不受規範的空間空間不受法律規範的影響 , 不僅僅是被你想要的國際貿易、網路、網路等等的東西所影響 。 還有你不想要的國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911事件的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 然而 , 那些居住在太空中的人 , 甚至可以攻擊你最具代表性的城市 , 一個九月的早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有百分之六十的四百萬美金被帶到資助911事件的機構中 , 其實已經通過了911事件摧毀的雙子星大樓 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播──能夠繞過它們的毒藥 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	不久前 , 不久後 , 歷史的規則就是權力的統治必須遵循 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象是全球化的權力 , 那麼 , 我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把統治者帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們眼前的數十年 , 將來會有更大或更小的動盪 , 我們能夠達成這個目標:把統治者帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說設立某種全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 這不太可能透過更多的聯合國機構來完成 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個方法 , 你可以將國際行動合法化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當談到全球空間的統治時 , 我猜這不會透過更多的聯合國機構的創建來實現 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 它會發生在強大的團體中 , 建立以條約為基礎的體制、條約協議 , 來治國全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始浮現 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 然而 , 強大到足以容納最強大的美國 , 如果有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:掙扎的開始去創造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道我們必須組成一個能夠將統治權帶到金融空間的機構來推動財務上的推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而g20就是這樣 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談它 , 就是 , 如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 在以條約為基礎的機構中 , 來填補這個治理空間 , 那麼 , 那些剩下的弱者會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下會再回來 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要在動盪中穿越這些騷動 , 我們的成功會很大程度上是依據我們的能力 , 把合理的治理帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這個開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是垂直轉移 , 也是橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 一直都是文明聚集在海上第一批在地中海附近的文明 , 近期在大西洋各地的後裔 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到一個基本的權力轉移 , 廣泛來說 , 遠離大西洋周圍的國家 , 到太平洋大西洋各地聚集的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這始於經濟實力 , 但這就是一直開始的方式 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他日益增長的政策中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這不是從西方移轉到東方 , 不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 值得一提的是 , 美國將在未來十年、十五年保留在地球上最強權的國家 , 但她掌握著權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 , 徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	五十年來 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 在這五十年間 , 我們有一個完全的單一世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個羅盤的需求 , 都必須要被華盛頓的位置給參考 , 一個世界最適合一個巨人 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這並非常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在興起的是歷史上更正常的案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極世界的出現
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	一直到現在 , 美國一直是我們這個世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保留最強權的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多極地世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	當然 , 我自己猜測 , 中國的權力建設中心是不平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在自由化經濟後 , 將社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論題目 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 你看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 漸漸地 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來就像十九世紀的歐洲一樣 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀:一個偉大的英國外交部長 , 神阿坎寧 , 用來形容它是 「 歐洲的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	當時有一個平衡 , 一個五等的平衡
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是玩到平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這個單向世界所主宰的時期 , 你的同盟國納托 , 華沙特 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定權力的兩極性意味著固定聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但有多種權力的兩極性意味著轉換和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會漸漸看到我們的同盟國並沒有固定不變 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國國務卿曾說過: 「 英國有共同的興趣 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會漸漸看到 , 即使我們在西方國家會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈圈 , 來和其他人結盟 , 如果我們想要讓世界各地的事情做起來 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方並不夠好 , 我們必須帶其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方最後一次嘗試自己這麼做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經到了400年後的開始--我說400年後--因為這是鄂圖曼帝國的終止--西方的權力、西方的制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家團結起來 , 它可以在世界各地提出和解 。
but that's no longer true .	但那不再是事實 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後的最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家集結了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織-問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須打電話給其他人 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須達到超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做一個預測 , 這可能更讓人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經到了四百年的終點 , 那時西方的權力已經夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們從來沒有參與過世界各地的和平活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 ? 為甚麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗下服役 , 在現今的聯合國指揮下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11個 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	最大規模的海軍海軍艦隊在處理索馬利海盜議題是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商業的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們不共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 和誰、當下 , 我們共享共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的角度來看世界現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 由於網路 , 由於人們在這裡談論的種類 , 一切都與萬物相連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是被關閉的 , 作為國家 , 作為個人 , 一個從來沒有這樣過的情況 , 從來沒有如此 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的關聯性 , 嗯 , 它總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交的重點在於管理國家之間的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切鎖在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 這是24小時後查爾斯迪加爾機場的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個崩盤
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的腳步有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都已深切地、深切地互相連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家獨自行動的概念 , 不和其他人連結 , 不和其他人合作 , 不再是可行的提案 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動不被侷限在自己身上 , 也不足以讓國家國家自己掌控自己的領土 , 因為國家以外的影響已經開始影響到他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我曾是英國最後一個小型帝國大戰的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家對於一件事的防禦 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍有多強壯 , 我們的海軍有多強壯 , 我們的盟友有多強壯 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是當敵人在牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談我的國家的防禦 , 我得要談談健康部長 , 因為大流行病對我的安全是威脅 , 我得要談談我的農業部長 , 因為糧食安全對我的保障是威脅 , 我得要談談談我的國家 , 我得要談談談我的產業部長 , 因為希臘基礎設施的脆弱性 , 對於我們的敵人來說 , 如同我們從網路戰開始時所看到的──我得要談談談我的家鄉──我得要談談談談我的國家 , 在我的國家中 , 那些被直接發生的國家──在我們的國家──在我們的家中 , 住在很有可能發生 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是這樣 , 一個國家的安全只是對士兵及其國防部很重要 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力可以鎖定它的機構 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直構建 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直升降 , 專門化的任務 , 指令結構完全有錯誤的結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業中知道我們這個時代的範例結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你網絡的能力 , 不論在你的政府或外部都很重要 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	以下是艾希登的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順帶一提 , 不要問我第一條法律和第二條法則 , 因為我還沒發明過 ; 如果有第三條法則 , 聽起來總是比較好 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三個法則是 , 在現代 , 每件事都與萬物相連 , 最重要的是你能做什麼 , 就是你能和他人一起做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點是--不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍事上的註冊 , 不論你是企業--你的 「 信任點 」 , 你的交際點 , 你的交際點 , 你的能力 , 你與他人網絡的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你明白在工業上 , 政府不會
but now one final thing .	但現在有了最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的話 , 女士們先生們也就是我們現在被關在一起 , 以一種前所未有的方式被關在一起 , 那麼這也是我們彼此之間的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 已經把我們視為國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我是安全的 ; 我的同盟國 , 像是北約 , 比他們同盟國更強大 , 我是安全的 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結的出現 , 以及大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人有著命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是個外交官在1970年代與日內瓦的蘇聯聯談判時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們明白我們和他們分享了命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方意識到零和遊戲無法運作
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人分享了命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東地區和平的其中一個偉大的障礙就是雙方 , 無論是以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 都不明白他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	突然間 , 女士們先生們 , 一直以來 , 那些有遠見的詩人和詩人的提議 , 變成我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰.唐恩的偉大詩人
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要給誰留鐘聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是孤島 」 。
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它說: 「 每個男人的死都影響我 , 為了我涉入人類 , 不要向誰求鐘聲 , 它會為我鈴聲 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•唐恩而言 , 道德的建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 我們生存的方程式的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找長壽和健康的路徑 , danbuettner和團隊研究了世界上的 「 藍色區塊 」 , 社區裡的長者和維姆住在一起 , 並記錄了年齡 。 在tedxtc , 他分享了9個常見飲食和生活方式的習慣 , 讓他們持續在100歲前 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥的雙胞胎研究指出 , 大約只有10%的人平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制之內 , 被我們的基因所決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	剩下的90%則被我們的生活方式所獨裁 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能想出長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是阿特金斯飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	這是奧茲醫生告訴我們的 。
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是有很多困惑 , 真正能幫助我們活得更久 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉 , 還是應該吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品 , 你應該把他們帶走嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或逆水器呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否有成效 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性呢 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌合作 , 國家老化研究院合作 , 找出四個人口確認地理位置的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶一個專家團隊到那裡去 , 以方法方法來了解這些人的所作所為 , 來提煉跨文化的瓦解 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 那個幻覺是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要揭示一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽的問題 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你非常努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國5000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口統計 , 但很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為了長壽而寫程式 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為了所謂的成功而設計的 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起我大學的日子
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意味著你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那次演化的效應完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或是人類 , 在兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要做到100歲 , 你不只要有非常好的生活方式 , 你也要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以協助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到時 , 有99件事情可以讓我們變老 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	剝奪你腦中的氧氣短短幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀掉你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可能會堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來支撐 , 我們就能得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用一個 " t. " 我們在這裡談的是國家負債數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每8年一次輪流一次
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們自己轉移到那邊時 , 就會造成傷害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數的速度增長
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹專輯的日子 , 我們會在錄音帶上做複製 , 讓我們的朋友複製那錄音帶 , 很快的 , 很快的 , 這個世代就聽起來像垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度比一個12歲的人要快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事實是最好的科學告訴我們人體、身體、身體的能力大約90年 , 女性多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線的某個地方 , 我們在桌上留下了大約12年的美好 。
these are years that we could get .	我們能得到的這些年 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 多年以來 , 大多免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失蹤年齡最好的方法 , 就是看看全世界實際體驗到的文化 , 在那裡 , 人們的年齡要比我們高出100倍 , 比我們高出10倍 , 平均壽命是十幾年 , 中年的死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色區域距離義大利海岸約125英里 , 位在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有高地 , 一個叫做nuoro省 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡的這個區域是男人最長壽的 , 大約比我們在美國這裡的比我們多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不只達到100歲 , 而且還有非凡的處女 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	102歲的老人仍舊騎自行車去工作 , 雜碎的木材 , 可以比他們年輕60歲 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上是回到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的青銅時代文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的有害 , 它們很大程度上是牧羊人 , 這種情況會定期、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎 , 以牠們能帶到田地的食物為基礎 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做cata音樂 , 用杜魯姆小麥做成的一種起士 , 用草食品動物做成的一種起士 , 所以在omega-3脂肪酸上 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 另一類的葡萄酒比世界上任何已知的酒都高出三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們如何組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國這裡 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看一下廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 年紀越大 , 你就越能得到你所擁有的平等 , 你就越能為之讚頌智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 不是看到運動說明游泳日曆 , 而是看到月曆的百歲人瑞 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 不僅對你的年齡父母有益 , 還能讓他們跟家人親近 , 大約是四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示 , 這對那些家庭的孩子有益 , 死亡率和疾病的比率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現地球另一端的第二個藍色區塊 , 位於東京南邊約800英里 , 位在俄亥俄州的阿基拉哥 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北部地區 , 這是世界長壽的地點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的雌性族群被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	它是一個人們擁有世界上最長壽命的殘疾人士的地方 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很久 , 很快地在睡眠中死去 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性行為之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比美國人平均壽命長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國的百歲人瑞數是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	結腸癌和乳癌的比率是美國的五分之一 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比率是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化產生了這些數字的事實 , 強烈地表示他們有東西可以教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面滿是大量有色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃的豆腐大約是美國人吃的八倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的食物更顯著 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略可以避免過度飲食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們從小盤子裡吃東西 , 所以他們每坐下都會傾向少吃點卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 你可以在談話時無意識地吃東西 , 他們會在櫃台上服務 , 把食物送走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個3000歲的年齡 , 我覺得這是最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是由康乃斯所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那個飲食是眾所周知的哈拉、哈蒂奇、布丁飲食 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小小的說 , 在他們吃飯之前 , 提醒他們在胃裡吃東西時 , 不要再吃東西了 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	大概要半小時 , 才能從腹部傳到大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停止百分之八十 , 它能幫助你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有一些社會建構 , 可以與長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致死 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地出生在琉球 , 你生在一個系統 , 一個自動擁有半打朋友的系統 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為moai 。 如果你在一個你預期會碰到運氣的moai身上 , 如果你遇到壞事 , 孩子會生病 , 家長會死 , 你總是有人背著 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起九十七年了
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們把成年人的生活分成兩個部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休時的椅子 , 或是下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一個字正是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯了 , 意思是 「 你早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的karate大師來說 , 他的生計帶著這種武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫來說 , 一週要捕魚 , 三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際上給了我們一個問卷給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們在文化上非常敏銳 , 那些把問卷寫下來的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的基金會是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老婦女來說 , 她的生計只是她的曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半前分離
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	然後她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區塊 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們在明尼蘇達的草原上查看 , 實際上 , 百歲人瑞的比例非常高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有離開的年輕人
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長壽的族群 , 位於加州的洛馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	保守主義者是保守的方法 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五慶祝安息日的安息日 , 直到星期六日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱它為 「 24小時的庇護所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 向他們傳達非凡的長壽 , 相較於說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	這裡的美國 , 平均每位女性平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位先生婦女來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差異更高的是男性的發音 , 她們的壽命比美國男性的平均壽命長約11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約70 , 000人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 而且我認為這是最高的說明了這個藍色區塊計畫的前景 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙人、亞洲人
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一組非常小的生活方式習慣 , 他們一生中大部分時間都遵循儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中採取他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章 , 不是29節 , 上帝談到樂子和種子 , 再來在斯坦尚尼亞談到綠色植物 , 可能缺少的就是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們很認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們多忙 , 工作壓力有多大 , 孩子需要被驅使 , 他們停止一切 , 把焦點放在他們的神、他們的社交網路上 , 接著 , 在宗教中 , 天性就是大自然的散步 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這股力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 權力是每週完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他的冒險家相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一場演員的派對 , 你不會看到人們在跳舞或滾動關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是他們談論他們的下一大自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會以深刻且可測的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓艾爾斯沃斯沃罕默默默默無名 ,
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	艾爾斯沃爾漢九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁 , 但當一位承包商要六千美金來建造一個隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我自己來做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他出海了水泥 , 到處拖著竿子 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預測 , 也許 , 在第四天他最後進到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不像桌子上的那個人 , 開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲時 , 他仍然每個月進行二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 從他的早晨開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡放到板子上 , 扔起公雞尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在雙胞胎城市這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她從抬起重量的那一天開始
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在她的根部有色人種 , 1994年的卡迪拉克賽維爾 , 淚流下聖貝納迪諾的高速公路 , 在那裡 , 她仍然為七個不同的組織做志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19趟硬體探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你遇過的人 , 在撒哈拉沙漠遊走他的腳踏車 , 卻沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比和瑪格•狄頓一起開槍更駭人 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中的共同點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做了什麼事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們想辦法將它歸結為9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們從此以後就再做了兩次藍色區域探險 , 而這些共同的譴責者是真的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我將要在這裡說個笑話 , 沒有任何運動 , 至少我們看待運動的方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們建立了自己的生命 , 這樣他們不斷地被推入身體活動中 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人 , 她們每天都坐在地板上 , 30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每趟去商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家的房子都有一趟散步 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以按下去做雅茲工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想把蛋糕混合起來 , 他們就用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機燃燒的卡路里和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 這是他們享受的東西 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實的方式就是脫離認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向有個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來設定自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間來降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的先生祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的傳奇 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在急促或壓力外界時 , 會觸發一種叫 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 這種反應和一切都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 將那發炎狀態變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有目的性的詞彙 , 像okinawans 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你人生中最危險的兩年就是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感 , 並且在他們的生活中活躍 , 那是價值約七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天喝一點點 , 不是很難賣給美國人 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	牠們傾向以植物為基礎的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是大量的豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而他們有策略可以避免過度飲食 , 小事在適當的時機讓他們遠離桌面 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老化父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於屬於一個信仰型族群 , 價值四到十四年的額外預期壽命 , 如果你每個月做四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就是活躍地把自己包圍在對的人身上 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗明罕研究中得知如果你三個好朋友都過胖有50%的機會會過重
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 隨著時間就會有可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你朋友的休閒想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或是玩曲棍球 , 自行車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但他們吃得不太好 , 他們吃得沒錯 , 他們很投入 , 並且信任和信任 , 值得信任 , 這會對時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食不管用 , 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食可供超過2%的人口使用
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常是從一月開始的 ; 它們通常是十月來的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽 , 沒有短期的術語在藥丸或其他任何東西上 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最顯著的事 , 為你的生活加上更多年 , 為你的日子 。 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水會導電 ; 從清晰的角度 , 到切換的不透明的窗口 ; 一個會製造音樂的水母 。 所有東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜莫納說:該是玩的時候了 。 mota帶領我們踏上一趟驚喜和酷酷的新材料之旅 , 暗示著我們要知道他們對實驗有什麼好處 , tinker , 很有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的爺爺用腳踏車和一台洗衣機建造了一台車 , 這樣他就可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解到事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何被製造 , 所以我們可以建立和修復它們 , 或最少知道要買什麼東西的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這些做法在二十世紀後半失去了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼模型正帶著這種知識 , 關於事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何被我們的生活所組成 , 我相信我們需要帶它們到下一個層級 , 到達組成的元件 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們如何生產的 。
