but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些驚人又光彩的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀 , 可以導電的顏料 , 可以改變顏色 , 可以發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們能畫出電路 , 而不是使用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我拿著這個小小的例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 來對我的皮膚做出反應 , 打開這個小光線 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電油墨已經被藝術家使用 , 但近期的發展指出 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一張acrylic的紙 , 用無顏色的光源注入微粒 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	意思是 , 一般的丙烯酸鹽只會在邊緣散光 , 這一顆會照亮整個表面 , 當我打開周圍的燈光時 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的兩個已知應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而熱電顏料會在特定的溫度變化顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放在一個熱板子上 , 溫度只比模擬高一點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這種材料的其中一項原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它指出當內容物夠酷喝的時候 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	在幾年內 , 它們會在我們日常使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛天車科幻小說向我們保證 , 但我們能有改變顏色的牆壁 , 依照溫度、鍵盤來滾動 , 窗戶變成不透明的開關 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以我是社會科學家藉由訓練 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造者 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物的運作方式以及它們的製造方式 , 也因為我相信我們應該要更深入了解構成我們的世界的構成要素 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的複合體了解不夠多 , 我們的未來會被組成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料很難在微量上取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 很少人會說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 他們主要存在於貿易秘密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , kirsty男孩和我開始了一個專案 , 我們稱為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是個網站 , 我們 , 和其他任何想要加入我們的人 , 共享實驗 , 發佈資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在何時隨地貢獻 , 並收集資源 , 像是其他像我們一樣的研究論文和課輔等 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為智慧型材料的大型、集體的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料如何運作 , 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解和使用的東西最後會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、我們穿的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直是微乎其微的燃料 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當他們發表一篇論文時 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他對化學沒有任何經驗 , 直到那時 , 讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的自造者空間中複製了實驗 , 只用了現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 他甚至製作了自己的旋渦混合器 , 根據另一位科學家/麥克斯的課輔 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦接著在網路上發表他的研究結果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過的所有東西 , 且沒有用 , 讓其他人可以研究並重製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦主要的創新形式 , 是把一個實驗用在大學裡的有裝備的實驗室裡 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重製它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己製作 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這項工作 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程 , 改進 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想要提到她的計畫目標的例子是要強調材料的表現特質 , 同時要把焦點放在建造者的創造力和技能上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子組件非常強大 , 在於它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但限制在它們的設計中 , 會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的作法是建立一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 使我們免於預先設計的限制 , 藉由教導我們這些材料本身 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面有一些銅膠帶連接著一個mp3播放器和磁鐵
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的馬賽洛柯爾荷研究 , 漢娜用大量的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造家一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製和複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的工藝作品 , 以及她共享發現的事實 , 打開了一連串新的可能性 , 這些可能都是審美和創新的 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們從熱情和好奇心中創造出來 , 我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不規則的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究者就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出真正能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在必須了解電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的大型主體 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人夢想能在家中有一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先驅知識是確保我們未來能有言論的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠我們的眼睛來指導我們 , 即使我們只能看到前面和後面那些車子 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 了解它們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路線 ? 珍妮佛•華麗想像一個沒有事故的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛healey:如果車子可以說話 , 意外可能會避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教代表和好運魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛著我們所知道的事實 , 就是我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是十六到十九歲美國人死亡的主要成因 , 導致死亡和百分之七十五的意外都跟毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒人能肯定 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我是個年輕的司機 , 在高速公路上 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈繼續下去 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這個傢伙正在慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不是在放慢速度 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 停下來 , 停在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	剛剛到65歲到零了 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上滑行 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺abs踢進去 , 車子仍在前進 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道不會停下來 , 空中袋子部署了 , 車子總算很快 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停了 , 我想我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想我們可以改變開車經驗 , 讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望各位能稍微思考一下開車的經驗是什麼樣子的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 。 關上門 。 你在玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你真的無法直接感知你周圍的世界
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 ,
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導向一部分看不見的道路 , 在其他金屬巨人之中 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	可以嗎 ? 而你只需要指導你就是你的雙眼 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的眼睛不是真的為這個任務設計的 , 但後來人們請你做一些事情 , 例如 , 你想做一條車道改變 , 他們問你第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿掉 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別再看你要去哪裡 , 轉身 , 檢查你的盲點 , 開車到馬路邊 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是開車的安全方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看這邊還是我看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上要做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們忽略了一些
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺出錯或遲到 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換的資料 , 我們將能看到不只是前面三輛車 , 還有三輛車後面 , 右邊和左邊 , 全都同時 , 鳥瞰視野 , 我們將能夠真正看到那些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙走了多快或停了多遠 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	藉由計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為那是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 , 有了汽車 , 並不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是有固定位置和速度的三維物體 。
they travel down roads .	沿著道路行駛
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在出版前的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理的預測 , 預測車子在不久的將來會在哪裡 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使當你在你的車上 , 一些摩托車騎士來了 ! 時速85英里 , 車道插進去--我知道你有過這種經驗--那位男士不是 「 無所不在 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙大概在前半小時都在路上
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英哩後 , 有人看過那傢伙 , 一旦有車看到那傢伙 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他在地圖的位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你一定會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳朵裡悄悄地說些什麼 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測車輛的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說相當不錯 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從一些簡單的東西開始 , 像是分享我們車子之間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有gps和攝影機在我的車裡 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 知道我在哪裡 , 以及我要走多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子位置 , 和他們要去的位置 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車輛也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確的知道自己在哪裡 , 有點模糊的知道其他車輛在哪裡 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車分享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以準確地告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 當模糊的估算加起來會發生什麼事 , 甚至在光線交通中 , 當汽車只是分享gps資料時 , 我們已經把這個研究移出電腦模擬出來 , 移到機器人測試床上 , 現在在這些機器人身上有實際的感測器:音響攝影機、gps , 以及在後備系統中普遍存在的二維雷射測器 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還會附著一個分散的短距離通訊電台 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此來到時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們就能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在正在將越來越多的機器人加入混合當中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天器時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 這就是預測模型幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子全都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會注意那些包裹 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	優先考慮一個看起來有點偏離軌道的人 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要離開了 , 你知道怎麼走 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要警示哪些駕駛者 , 才能脫身 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	而我們想做的是如何能警告所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車子怎麼能悄悄的說: 「 你需要走出去 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人真的有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急狀況中做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始做分離的研究 , 做駕駛狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用三部攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛是向前看 , 向下看 , 在電話上看 , 或是喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外的發生 , 我們可以預測誰、誰、哪一輛車 , 在最好的位置上 , 搬出路上 , 來為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今這些科技的存在
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己願意分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我覺得這是一個非常讓人不安的想法 , 這個想法就是我們的車子會看著我們 , 和我們談到其他車子 , 我們會在一片八卦的大海中走下去 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看著你的車 , 我並不真的知道你是怎麼想的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以談論我們的背後 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	請你思考一下 , 如果你真的不想在你身後分心的青少年知道你在煞車 , 你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做對每個人最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車八卦關於你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬•霍金實現他前往太空的夢想 , 藉由一起飛行到大氣中 , 並在0g中體驗到無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的演講、空間、科技、宇宙、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在stephenhawking上以g0為中心
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	在座認識我的人知道我有多熱衷於打開太空前線 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給予世界萬有引力的專家--無重力的經歷 , 真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴大家這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 穿越了基因組學的考古獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一組在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一百個基因組 , 被定序為一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那事件的椅子
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇見了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力中 , 進入zerog 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 地球上唯一能體驗zerog的方法 , 其實是和平行飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 你沒有體重25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再 , 再而三地
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力──太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人──多久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣佈要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一家公司的飛行器操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那個傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他也想去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了一場新聞大會 , 我們宣佈我們的意圖要做一個zerog拋物線 , 給他25秒的zerog 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼想上去做這個 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常動人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正不斷增加 , 被災難消滅......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為 , 如果它不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在美國太空總署的車輛內部 , 進入zerog飛機後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們募到150 , 000美元捐款給和我們一起飛行的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位ted成員 ,
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他血液中的po2 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們把一切都設定在緊急情況下 , 天知道 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 在那裡 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我和我的夥伴拜倫.立克騰伯和我小心地把他吊成zerog 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力是真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 然後我們說 , 去吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二次拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們真的在向艾薩克•牛頓爵士漂浮一顆蘋果因為霍金教授在劍橋舉辦了同樣的椅子伊薩克•牛頓教授
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	還有第七個 , 第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這位男子看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們一生中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們在史詩般的冒險旅程中
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家大衛•博林斯基在細胞內展現了三十分鐘的驚人動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫學插畫家 , 我從一個稍微不同的觀點
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在觀察 , 自從長大以來 , 藝術和真與美的表達方式和科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩件很棒的事都是在它們的右邊 , 它們都有很美妙的事物 , 會讓它們成為真與美的理想 , 可以被科學和數學所探討 , 就像是科學家會想約會的理想中的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真理的表達方式是令人敬畏的事物 , 意味著它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強而有力的理想 , 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 它們有時是很有用的 , 在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在可以放幾張照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美往往對不在科學領域的人來說是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是一種形容美的事物 , 通常只有當你了解語言和語法時 , 才能夠取得它 , 它才能夠被描述出來 , 那些研究對象的語言和語言 , 才會被表達出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字進化而來 , 這些是非常困難去理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被教導我的醫學插畫師以來 , 我試著要做的是 , 他是一位雕塑家和我的視覺導師 , 我想要找出一種方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 藉由使用動畫、用圖片、用圖片 , 來描述故事 , 這樣人們不見得能被帶給別人看 , 且能被教導 , 且能被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常都沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學到的都是受測者 , 當中有真與美 , 但他們被教導的方式是被拿來做比較的 , 被認為是事實和美不見得都很明顯的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 你把雞煮熟 , 直到香味剛不見 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放接受教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我和哈佛大學的robertlue接到電話 , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 幾年前 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否會有興趣 , 並願意真正改變哈佛的醫療和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始著手一項計畫 , 探索細胞 , 來探索分子和細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生可以了解一個更大的圖片 , 可以把這些事實掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	牠們的心智圖像可能是一座大型、破壞 , 非常複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 世界各地都很羨慕奈米技術專家 , 自我引導、強大、精準、精確的裝置 , 都是用胺基酸做成的弦 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械能驅動細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	細胞如何複製 , 驅動我們的心臟
they power our minds .	它們驅動了我們的心靈 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是想找出我們如何把這個故事變成一個動畫將成為哈佛的生物visions的中心這個網站是哈佛大學為分子和細胞生物學學生所設立的一個網站他們將除了所有教科文學資訊以外 , 把所有內容都視覺化 , 這樣這些學生將細胞內化為真與美 , 並且能夠研究這些觀念 , 以至於他們的想像力會被激發出來 , 如此一來 , 他們的想像力會被激發出來 , 使他們能夠發出新的生命 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬細胞在微血管下流動 , 它們正在觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們從毛細管壁上的細胞取得資訊 , 它們被吸收到 , 它們被吸收到 , 這些資訊在外面的某處 , 傳遞著發炎 , 在那裡 , 它們看不到和感知到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓他們停下來 , 造成他們內化 , 他們得要做出所有會造成他們改變形狀的各個部分 , 並試著脫離這個毛細管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家和數據庫模型一起研究原子精確的分子 , 並找出它們的移動方式 , 找出它們的做法 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想辦法以真誠的方式實現它隱含了當時的狀況 , 但事實並非如此 , 細胞裡的擁擠會阻礙視覺的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一部三分鐘的讀者消化版 , 我們製作的這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是個持續進行的計畫 , 將要再過四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這點 , 看看細胞製造這些步驟的路徑 , 它們被稱為 「 kinesins 」 , 採用的是相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請繼續看電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器 , 真的相當驚人 , 它們是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	他們互相傳遞信息
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內不同的事情發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會真的製造它在果蠅身上所需要的零件 , 從讀取基因的分子所帶來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率真的很大 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 kinesin 」 , 他拉起一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質的包裝 , 到細胞中任何需要的位置 , 不論是用細胞膜 , 不論是用器官 , 不論是用來建造東西或修復某物 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西跑來跑去 , 現在 , 在你們的一百兆個細胞中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以不論你有多懶惰的感覺 , 你本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你回家時 , 我希望各位思考一下這個 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	並思考一些我們正在學習的關於細胞力學的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞清楚了所有這些 , 相信我 , 一旦我們搞清楚了到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠對我們的健康有很大的控制權 , 用我們未來世代所做的事 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能夠用這個來發現更多的真相 , 以及更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 非常驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 已經足夠意識到細胞需要它們的協助 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 , 使細胞做出它需要做的事
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	他們同心協力 , 協助我們的身體 , 巨大的實體 , 它們永遠看不到正常運作 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受剩下的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓計劃在她的旅行車上住了一年 , 看到了這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症開始 , 以及她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她身為美國無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝琪•布蘭頓:我是無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個很有好奇心的人 , 所以身為記者的22年 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做到的其中一件事就是成為隱形的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	在我父親在同年二月去世後 , 我辭去了報紙編輯的工作 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我這麼做時 , 我有很多事想要去感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 然後我決定住在旅行車上一年 , 做這件事就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓 , 旋轉推車和我的露營裝載到1975年雪佛蘭旅行車上 , 開車進入日落 , 完全沒有意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會等同於生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一片粉碎 , 擁有一個人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我無法意識到 , 其他人的負面觀念能對我們的現實造成多快的影響 , 如果我們讓它發生 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車上很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 定期吃飯
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	而我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著我父親的憤怒和憂鬱症進來了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 而我必須得到一份全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個很溫和的春天變成很熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	任何地方都不可能停車 , 不用很明顯地 , 我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過車廂的一扇開窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	小狗進入日照護 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	不論何時 , 我都會在辦公大樓和卡車站使用員工淋浴 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或是我在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間在廂型車內的溫度很少降到華氏80度以下 , 讓睡眠變得困難或不可能 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	數小時內在我的冰胸裡冰塊融化了 , 相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起要找公寓 , 或負擔不起公寓 , 讓我能擁有羅特威爾和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我病得太重 , 無法在晚上走50英尺到公共廁所時 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣進來時 , 溫度降低到冰點之下 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都停在不一樣的地方 , 這樣我會避免被警察注意到 , 陷入困境 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感到自己無法掌控自己的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道是何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 到一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在旅行車裡 , 帶走我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒改變 。 我的智商尚未下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華 , 我的完整性 , 我的價值觀 , 關於我的一切都維持一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎麼地改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我旋轉得越來越深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 , 三天沒洗澡
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排在隊伍中的人一樣迷戀和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或喝醉 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當有幾個流浪漢意識到 , 包括一位前大學的教授 , 他們說: 「 你不無家可歸 , 你為什麼真的在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人並沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我也這麼做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著教授聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的遊民沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診療給了我憂鬱症的反應讓我自殺了 。 我記得我當時在想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅素 , 她是全國知名的記者 , 一直在全國電視上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做一個演講電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•羅素 , 前主持人 「 遇見新聞 」 時 , 談到我的寫作 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪超市的旅行車裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為它到了哪裡 , 我是個作家 , 還是一個流浪女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到了提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	然後我站在那裡 。 然後我重新讀我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回了田納西州
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友一起住在旅行車和沙發衝浪之間 。
and i started writing again .	然後我又開始寫
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了隔年的夏天 , 我還是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得了獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 生活在他們的車上 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續污名化並犯罪生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要是保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇過一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以戰勝任何事物如果有希望的話
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們把錢給下一個你認識的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡 , 他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或是他們在任何時候的生活情況是什麼 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在一個沃爾瑪超市的旅行車裡 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , 梅秋.維拉維拉迪亞帶我們走過全國的大膽計畫 , 提高生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著大量的坦白、有趣 , 以及非常有效的談到保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaidya:康德先生如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有許多許多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫或貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕育兒童健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭計劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:到孩子那兒 , 去找母親 , 然後跟上家庭計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是兒童死亡率 , 你也需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個小孩成長率極高 , 佔3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一個醫生來開藥 。 」 我們只有非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們並沒有把 「 不 」 當作答案 ; 我們把 「 不 」 視為問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女性 , 在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做了很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只涵蓋了全國20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	另外百分之八十的人會做什麼 , 讓他們獨處 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找你們看到的普通人
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標誌下面 , 我希望他們還沒做到這點 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那時我們比可口可樂要大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的對象就是我們選的對象 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客總是對的 , 且他們很棒 , 他們自己在做家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥丸和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 就這樣 。 我們去找那些被視為問題的原因的人 , 成為解決方案的原因 。

and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教教會相當強壯 , 泰國人都是佛教徒 。

over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過四十萬人被教導關於家庭計劃 , 用新的字母a、出生、保險套、iud、v為血管切除術 。

in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石不會變成這樣 , 所以保險套就是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個微型信用計劃 , 整理它的婦女說: 「 我們只想借給實行家庭計劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們那裡拿出貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	經過35/36年 , 仍在持續進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 但它是個基金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營這個組織 , 由村民自己經營 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也缺乏信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是商業社群提供的
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家、小商人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是透過企業企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 這件事完成了 。

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你可以借錢之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信條一定是人權 。

and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你一定要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	這是我們所謂的 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 這樣 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功地與企業合作 。

and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 終於在教育上 , 我們想把學校改造成一個地方 , 讓每個人終身都能學習中心 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會感覺像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你一次微笑 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒.瑞納多.羅馬 , 智慧型手機驅動的迷你機器人 , 可以和你一起在散步上移動 , 將一杯咖啡滑過桌面 , 用可編程的表達方式做出反應 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive想解決的問題:我和其他二十個呆瓜在romotive迷戀解決的問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想建造一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不論你是八歲或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不但真的負擔得起 , 還必須是人們真正想要回家 , 還能在他們的孩子身邊買東西的東西 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo的機器人使用你已經知道的裝置 , 把你的iphone當成他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個能讓150美元的wi-fi可觀及電腦可觀的機器人 , 這大約是過去這類型機器人的成本的百分之一 。
