you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 她有一支iphone , 她的媽媽買了她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那女孩可以拿她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送電子郵件給祖母 , 住在國家的另一端 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩躲藏品玩躲藏品 , 每天晚上十五分鐘 , 否則她可能一年只能看到孫女一到兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的議題 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一位工程師 , dom , 在一個週末建成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	建立在一個叫blockly的google開放架構上 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這讓你可以拖曳、丟下這些semantic代碼的積木 , 為你想要的機器人創造任何行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編碼來為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上你可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行 , 在現實生活中執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有你感到驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上每個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以所有這些wi-fi可感應的機器人其實互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以如此專注於建造每個人都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最引人注目的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們從人變為人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中有一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己的想像力的一種表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我完全不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們確實知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美金或一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	現今個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 比如romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們等不及要幫你們全部機器人 , 我們等不及要看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進分子伊莎貝•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有在這場演說中的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 , 非常可怕 , 能來到這裡是最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡告訴各位一些關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我喜歡
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相更真實 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個說故事的人 , 我想要傳達一個比真實更真實的東西 , 關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些困擾 , 直到我最後寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的奧秘 , 所以我寫下巧合 , 預兆 , 情緒 , 夢想 , 大自然的力量 , 魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我活在匿名的生活中 , 直到2006年2月 , 當時我帶著奧運國旗在義大利的冬季奧運會 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為名人 。 現在人們在毛西的身上認得我 , 而我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我告訴各位我那四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	奧林匹克運動會的其中一位組織者打電話給我 , 說我被選為旗幟管理員之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆肯定這是一個錯誤認同的案例因為我是從運動員中得到的
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以走在體育場沒有助行器的附近 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次只有女性會帶著奧運旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女士 , 代表五大洲 , 還有三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一件制服 , 她說 , 並尋求我的衡量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對我自己有個遠景 , 在一個流利的大動脈中 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現我自己在渦輪 , 在那裡 , 熱情的群眾在80個奧運會隊伍的任何一人都在街上歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了在遊戲中競爭的一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪 , 一英寸的冰 , 風的力量 , 可以決定賽道或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼和堅定的心才會得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	渦輪的街道上滿是紅色海報宣佈奧運會的口號
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動我們 , 並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那是我書中角色需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議人士 , 冒險家 , 局外人和叛逆者 , 他們問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 並冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只製造好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了另一支旗熊:三位運動員 , 以及女演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩位有熱情心的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然還有許多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	而索馬利•媽媽 , 一位柬埔寨活動家 , 熱衷對抗童賣 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	在她14歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給一個妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信 , 和非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒她們免於愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們被迫每天收到五、十五個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被用電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這並不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但它離我所預期的米其林人西裝還很遠 。 不是壞的 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗幟師 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 美的普遍象徵和熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很渺小 , 很高 , 有著很深的標靶 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能有深色的棕色色 , 沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視訪問中問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直立著 , 我不製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有一些免費的建議 , 來自地球上最美麗的女性之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有怨氣 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有哀愁 , 沒有和自己說話 , 沒有偏遠 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	大約在午夜時分的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的機翼 , 大聲點擊者宣佈奧運旗 , 順帶一提 , 音樂開始於此 , 和從這裡開始的同樣的音樂 , aida遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前──她比我高一英尺 , 不算花花粉的頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩上拿著旗子 。 我在我的尖端拿著旗子 , 手上拿著旗子 , 這樣我的頭其實是在該死的旗幟底下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中我也會出現 , 雖然通常都在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想成為的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最好的四分鐘就是奧運體育館 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生在說這句話時會被冒犯 , 儘管我向他解釋 , 我們在私下做的事通常花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自服用 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個偉大時刻的所有按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記他們 , 什麼時候老年人會破壞我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著我心中的奧運這個關鍵字
so here's a tale of passion .	這是個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 地點是剛果tutsi難民營的監獄營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上百分之八十的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果一個死亡營 , 因為那些沒被殺死的人將死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪卓 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她是懷孕和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫受到折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知何故 , 她想讓她的七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 她生了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子割斷臍帶 , 然後用自己的頭髮來綁 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她把雙胞胎命名為 「 營地指揮官 」 , 以獲得他們的喜愛 , 並用黑茶來餵給他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡闖來強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她抓著她並拒絕放手 , 即使當他們拿著槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家族存活了16個月 , 接著 , 藉由非凡的運氣 , 以及一個美國年輕人的熱情心 , 薩夏夏查諾夫 , 她想辦法把她放在美國救援的飛機上 , 玫瑰色的地圖和她的九個孩子最後來到亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 在那裡 , 他們現在的生活和成長茁壯 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖圖 , 在斯瓦希里語中 , 代表偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書的主角很強壯也很有熱情的女性 , 像玫瑰色的女主角 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們組成 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性合作 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古代 , 在世界末日 , 在一個父權天主教和保守的家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪五歲時我是個狂熱的女性主義者雖然這個名詞還沒到智利所以沒人知道我到底怎麼了
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出高價 , 以及質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為每次我收到的鼓吹 , 我都能送到2 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒保羅在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會 , 我應該繼續前進 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有了難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒和今天在場的所有人而言 , 特權女性 , 但對世界上大部分的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫要婚姻早婚、賣淫、強迫勞動──她們有孩子不想要或不能餵飽 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們對自己的身體或人生沒有任何控制權 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被無罪殺害 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大多數西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我有嚴重的處境 , 缺乏男性 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義並不是死的 , 絕不是死的 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 對女神來說 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 " phen " 或 " venus " 或 " bimbo " 或 " 諸如此類 " 不管你怎麼想 " , 只要我們明白它的內容 , 我們支持它
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉一個村莊的小婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	2005年
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 她在三週假期時去了診所 , 擔任志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備清潔牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿是蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了好幾個小時接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人因為她有好幾顆腐爛的臼齒
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮了解到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔掉壞牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有為此授權 , 她從來沒有實踐過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很多風險 , 嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸好她還帶來了一些非口味 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有一顆勇敢且熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她在禱告中謀殺了一名禱告 , 並且在操作上前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家再抽出許多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人正和丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女子的臉看起來像個西瓜
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它腫到連眼睛都看不到 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣憤 , 威脅要殺美國人
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮很害怕她做過的事 , 但後來翻譯解釋病人的狀況和手術毫無關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她的丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有時間為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性像這樣生活著 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性從事世界上三分之二的勞動 , 但卻擁有不到全世界資產的1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水比男性少 , 如果薪水完全沒有 , 且她們仍然很脆弱 , 因為她們沒有經濟獨立 , 且她們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制她們自己的收入、繼承 , 以及自己的財產 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭大興盛 , 村落大聲繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女說話 , 解釋這塊土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐和賣掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新樹 , 澆水 , 一滴就掉下來 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五六年內 , 他們就有森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村落也被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最窮和最落後的社會 , 總是把女性放下來的那些人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給婦女的每一塊錢 , 每一塊錢就有20塊是給男性的方案 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 將會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性同心協力 , 連結、有知識 , 且受過教育 , 能將和平和繁榮帶給這個弱勢的星球 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是重大的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營世界 , 看看我們有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序合理嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 生命是被保存下來的 , 且生活品質是為每個人豐富的 , 不只為了有特權的人 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月時 , 我看到了費南多•博特羅在加州柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊除了背著波特羅作品的紐約畫廊也敢展出這幅畫因為主題是阿布格拉尼布監獄
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是酷刑的巨大畫作 , 以及權力的濫用 , 用的是大量的底特律風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法將那些影像從我的腦海或心中得到 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無罪的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力的濫用 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個族群中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 並強迫其他群體接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時都在改變 , 但它們總是對它們有益 , 在這個例子中 , 下游效應在經濟上是行不通的 , 在經濟上是行不通的 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子頂端向下滑到下方 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 在最底層
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男子最多的退休金 , 也有人可以虐待女人或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	透過性別、收入、種族和階級 , 我獲得了少數人的力量 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是成熟的 , 來對我們的文明做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 為了真正的改變 , 我們需要在世界管理階層中的女性能源 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要在權力的位置上有相當多的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的是有年輕心智的男性 , 當然
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是毫無希望的 , 我們必須等待他們離開 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要做選擇 , 我寧願擁有安格莉•瑪塔伊的戰士心 , 索瑪莉•媽媽、珍妮和玫瑰色的地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要讓它好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是有可能的 。 在這個房間裡環顧所有的知識、精力、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們脫掉粉絲 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在一個倫敦大小的城市中 , 三千萬份餐都被用盡了 。 但是所有的食物都從哪裡來 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論如何供養一個城市的日常奇蹟 , 並展現出古代食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳•史黛爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	然而卻很少被問及 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然的認為 , 如果我們進入商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時內進入這個劇院的門口 , 那裡就會有食物在等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 每天在倫敦大小的城市 , 足夠的食物都必須被生產、運送、買賣、煮飯、吃飯、丟棄 , 而那種類似的事情 , 每天都要發生在地球上的每座城市中 , 都市非常了不起 , 城市會被餵食 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的事物 , 忘記了這一點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要吃東西 , 其實我們對自然世界的依賴就像我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多人搬進城市 , 越來越多的自然世界被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的那塊 , 它是巴西馬托格羅索的黃豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但是我們少數人見過這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	漸漸地 , 這些景觀也不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人正在吃肉 , 以至全球每年三分之一的穀物被餵食到動物身上 , 而不是給我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	要是穀物要用到十倍的倍數來餵飽人類 , 如果它是先經過動物的話 , 那就不是很有效率的餵養方式 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個急迫的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們人口將有兩倍的人口住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	也估計 , 肉類和乳類消耗的量將會是兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和都市主義在手中升起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	在2050年之前 , 60億個飢餓的食肉動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們同時繼續下去 , 這是個我們很不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有九千萬公頃的雨林在創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然在同一時間 , 我們損失了相當於現有的耕地 , 供應出的鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來生產我們西方每一卡路里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管我們生產的成本很高 , 卻不重視食物 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前生產的食物有一半是被丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	結束這一切 , 在這漫長的過程結束後 , 我們甚至沒有辦法妥善餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人肥胖 , 同時 , 有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有一個是很合理的 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球百分之八十的食物交易是由五大跨國企業所掌控的 , 這是一張很嚴峻的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也在擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 這是個不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答一個稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開始 , 就在東邊的古老過程 , 也就是大家所知的肥沃土壤 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀很低 。
and it was also fertile .	它也非常肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約一萬年前就在這裡 , 兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和都市主義 , 發生在同一個地方 , 同時也發生在同一個地方 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市是緊密結合在一起的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先第一次發現穀物 , 生產出足夠大且穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些定居處是怎樣的 , 我們可以看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農地包圍著 , 被大型神廟複合體支配 , 像這個在烏爾的大型神廟複合體 , 事實上 , 神性化、中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神廟安排收割 , 聚集在穀物裡 , 提供給神 , 然後再提供神的穀物 , 神不會再吃回人 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活是由穀物和收穫所支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 在每一個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元前一個世紀 , 羅馬約有一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是如何自食其力的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是我所謂的 「 古老食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以取得海 , 這使得從很遠的地方進口食物是有可能的 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能在古代世界做到這一點的方法 , 因為要在道路上運送食物是非常困難的 , 這條路很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然很快就起飛了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地為卡拉奇和埃及引發戰爭 , 只為了在他們的穀物儲藏地上取得她的爪子 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 整個帝國的擴張真的是很漫長 , 被軍事化的購物速度真的很快 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬事實上 , 羅馬曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 從泰姆斯的底部進入 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場到了城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從他們向上提升到便宜 , 這是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以知道300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然對魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是河流來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然billingsgate , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的是很特別的 , 當你仔細想想 ,
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著手機到處遊走 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點沾沾沾自喜的魚在港口捕撈 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們就很少會移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是非常不同的故事因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦大部分的肉來自西北方 , 從蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就進來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位在上面 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從東安格利亞來到東北方
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女子這樣做 。 總之 , 鳥兒帶著腳走進來 , 用小畫布保護著 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞到廉價商店的東端時 , 那是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它叫做家鄉 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下在工業時代之前所建造的任何城市地圖 , 你可以追蹤進來的食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	其實你可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造 , 兩者是透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前的人生中 , 你在星期五去買你的魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一能買到食物的地方 , 也能賣掉的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面 , 你可以看到生活在這樣的城市是非常困難的 , 不知道你的食物從何而來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐的機會 , 可能是早三天就在你的窗外流出 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 也是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的影像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被屠殺從視力和心靈中 , 在鄉下的某處被屠殺 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並通過鐵路來到城市 ,
and this changes everything .	而這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首次在任何地方種植大城市是可行的 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去都市受到地理限制 ; 過去他們必須透過非常困難的實體手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理環境中被有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	正如你從這些倫敦地圖所看到的 , 在火車來臨的90年後 , 火車從一個小小的blob開始 , 很容易被動物帶進腳上 , 如此之類的 , 到一個很大的稀釋 , 很難和任何人一起吃飯 , 無論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 火車來了車後 , 真的是這個過程的結尾 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	是整個城市的最終解放從任何明顯與大自然的關係中
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市沒有氣味 , 沒有氣味 , 沒有氣味 , 肯定沒有人 , 因為沒有人夢想能在這樣的地景中行走 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物而做的是他們拿到車子 , 開車到郊區某處的箱子 , 回來一週的購物 , 想知道地球上要怎麼處理 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這一刻 , 我們與食物和城市的關係 , 完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有過去的食物是中心 , 城市的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	曾經是社交活動 , 購買和銷售食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會煮飯 , 現在只要加水 , 或一點點蛋如果你在做蛋糕之類的
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只要在包裝上讀到後面的標籤
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是珍貴它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食品系統的一個偉大的諷刺 , 是他們已經讓他們所承諾的事變得更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	透過在任何地方、任何地方建立城市 , 它們其實已經將我們與最重要的關係給隔絕了 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	同時 , 它們也讓我們依賴系統 , 只有它們能夠傳遞 , 就像我們所看到的 , 它們是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯更問他自己
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的書《烏托邦》的首映
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列的半獨立城邦 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉的話 , 一天的走向 , 每個人基本上都是農作物 , 在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 一起吃共用餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以爭辯說 , 食物是烏托邦的基本訂定原則 , 儘管更多從來沒有這樣架構過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 " 烏托邦 " 遠景 , 埃本納默斯克韋茲的 " 花園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:半獨立的城市 , 大都市的小團塊 , 周圍有可耕作的土地 , 加入了鐵路的彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視力的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建立起來 , 但和默斯克韋茲的這個願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦的想法的問題他們是烏托邦人
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘文中有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是指一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的事物 。 這是個想像的事物 。 我們不可能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類深層的難題 , 讓它變得不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西托邦 , 來自古希臘人 , 「 simtos 」 為了食物 , 以及 「 托波斯 」 等地 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到 , 我們可以把食物當成一個真正強大的工具--一個概念性的工具 , 設計的工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以 , 如果我們要這麼做 , 希托邦可能會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我想這看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 , 這只是狗臉上的表情
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	無論如何 , 這是生活的中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們為此花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會中食物應有的位置 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的景象 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順帶一提 , 這些人也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 想著前方 , 計畫著誰可以盯著一堆生菜 , 並且真正認得他們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這類人 , 我們就不可能有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選擇這個 , 是因為這是一個男人在買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡、食物在當地種植的市場 ,
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社會生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這些 , 你就不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物也是地景的一部分 , 不只是零和的商品 , 在不明顯的地獄之中 , 還會出現 。
cows with a view .	牛帶著一個觀點
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積如雨後春筍般 ,
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把整個東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們被告知有關食物和種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫凱文的植物 , 或許是植物屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類計畫試圖將我們與大自然重新連結是極其重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦是種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上就是認識到 , 西托邦已經存在於每個地方的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是加入它們 , 用食物來當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們將不再把城市視為大型、大都市化、無生產力的blobs , 就像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 看成是有生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免地連結在一起的 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更加思考永續發展 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖對我來說 , 是我們需要做的思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	將食物塑造我們生活的方式重新概念化 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最好的圖像是從650年前
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是ambrogiolorenzetti的《好政府的寓言》
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市和鄉村之間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這個訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家就會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問大家 , 阿姆布洛吉歐•洛倫澤提如果他今天畫了這張圖 , 會畫什麼畫 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會是什麼樣子 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個急迫的問題
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採用這個想法 , 我們可以把食物當作一種強而有力的工具 , 來讓世界變得更好 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在二十一世紀 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯從慈悲憲章的幾週後 , 探究了宗教的角色:它的教條是否會分裂我們 ? 還是它會團結我們共同的好事 ? 她會重新審視能驅動世界的信仰 , 重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年、暴力事件 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們復活黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教的歷史學家 , 我變得急切地意識到同情心的核心 , 在所有主要世界的信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出自己的版本被稱為黃金法則
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會以正面的版本出現 , 「 永遠在你想要對待自己時 , 去對待別人 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做什麼你不喜歡他們對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它是什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去除那痛苦 , 在其他人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調慈悲心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施黃金法則時 , 如混淆所言: 「 整天和一天 」 , 不只是一個在做你好事的疑問 , 然後回到貪婪和自我主義的生活中 , 而是整天都在做這件事 , 你將自己從你的世界的中心奪走 , 放下另一個人 , 然後你超越了自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶入所謂的神 , 涅盤 , 拉瑪 , 泰奧 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知道的自我意識存在的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活來說是如此的重要 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些美好的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖們聚在一起 , 他們爭論著廣告教義 , 或違背仇恨的議會 , 或對同性戀的仇恨行為之類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士說話時 , 有點自信的表情會越過他們的臉孔 , 因為人們常常想反而對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然也擊敗了運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地從我的書線研究帶我進入二十一世紀 , 讓我能在比我想像中更廣泛的觀眾面前演說 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 以至於我們對待所有人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 彷彿他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們有一個可行的世界 , 可以交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 是我們這個時代的一項偉大任務 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說 , 在那裡 , 人們可以和平共存 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有同理心的想像力 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有一個選擇 , 似乎對我來說
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出或強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 或者 , 我們可以回到拉比 。 耶穌的老年人希爾爾爾爾爾爾 , 當他被一個巴格蘭人請求總結整個猶太教義 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰居做任何事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	這就是托拉和其他一切只有評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	還有拉比和早期教會的父親說任何對仇恨和歧視的詮釋都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復原那種精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅僅是因為一種愛的精神把我們喚醒 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切發生 , 而且我們能用ted所引發的現代通訊來做到 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	對於我們所有伴侶的反應 , 我已經感到非常的震驚 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人將 「 憲章 」 用在近期的治癒分裂上 , 已經出現在新加坡社會 , 議會的某些成員也想在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將要有一個藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 並向他們展示 , 同情心也存在於所有藝術的根部 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區都在舉辦活動和討論 , 討論的是伊斯蘭的同情心核心 , 以及所有信仰 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停在那兒 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們走錯的地方 , 只專注於相信廣告教條 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會引發行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這個直到我死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續伴侶做兩件事 , 教育並刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們從同情心中輟學
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不懂慈悲 , 如果你只想的話 。
you also have to do it .	你也要做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能讓媒體參與 , 因為媒體協助解析我們其他人的一些刻板印象 , 將我們分隔開來 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的應用在教育者身上
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能感受到一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動力和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到它要求急性智能 , 而不只是感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者們 , 探討他們自己和其他人的傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	或許最重要的是 , 為了鼓勵一個關於不寬容的言論的敏感性 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這個憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏什麼 , 他們會覺得被賦予去挑戰不寬容的言論 , 不寬容的言論 , 不寬容的言論 , 來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 不寬容的言論 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們能改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把憲章放上網
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界中 , 一大堆鮑魚坐在一間房間裡 , 還在另一個亞歷山大宣言中 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹了我一個全新的思考和呈現想法的方法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted這麼棒的原因 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們一起加入 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎很荒謬 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但最後我想引用一個英國作家的說法 , 牛津作者我不常引用 , c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一件事讓我印象深刻 , 自從我在學校時讀到它 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛》中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他把愛情區別開來 , 當兩個人凝視 , 咒語 , 彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他將這點和友誼做比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁 , 就如同 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在一個共同目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 而是可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在調查中 , 我非常強烈地感受到 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起 , 一起合作共同達成一個共同目標 , 差異就會融化 。
and we learn amity .	而我們學會了野心 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 了解彼此 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacacaulay鬆開了風向 , 有時甚至超現實的旅程 , 朝羅馬•安德斯的補充品邁進 , 他向歷史城市致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	麥克阿瑟•格蘭特、藝術、書籍、城市、溝通、文化、娛樂、幽默、說故事故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫來更了解事物 。
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時我會畫很多圖 , 我仍然不明白我在畫什麼 。
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	那些對數位事物感到舒服的人 , 甚至沾沾自喜 , 想知道那段關係的人可能會覺得很有趣 , 知道那位以 「 工作方式 」 為名的人 , 同時為 「 理解 」 做準備 , 花了兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆電和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。
who knew about extension managers ?	誰知道延長經理呢 ?
i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直在做自己的延伸 , 甚至從來沒有想過要閱讀指示 , 但我終於想通了 。 我必須想通 , 因為邀請來了 , 提醒大家 , 沒有投影機 , 所以 , 帶著那些卡通不再必要 , 只是一些其他的溝通方式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談一些我很熟悉的東西 , 對這裡的許多人來說 , 都特別適合 , 或是我可以談談我真正關心的東西 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定用後者
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	我為什麼要關心羅馬呢 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在六零年代後半去羅德島設計學院研究建築 。
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運能花我過去一年、我第五年 , 在羅馬當學生 。 這改變了我的人生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	並不是最不理由的原因是我花了前四年住在家裡 , 每天開車進rsid , 開車回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了60年代 。 我讀到他們 , 我了解他們挺有趣的 。 我錯過了他們 , 但我在羅馬度過了那不平凡的一年 , 那是一個離我心頭不遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 每當有機會 , 我都會試著在其中做點什麼 , 或為它做點什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我也畫圖來幫助人們理解事物
things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們相信我了解的事物 。
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	這就是我作為一個插畫家的做法 , 這是我的工作 。
so , i'm going to show you some pictures of rome .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些羅馬的照片 。
i've made a lot of drawings of rome over the years .	這些年來 , 我畫了很多羅馬的圖畫 。
these are just drawings of rome . i get back as often as possible i need to .	這些只是羅馬的圖畫 。 我盡可能的回去 。
all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	所有不同的材料 , 各種不同的風格 , 各種不同的時間 , 從草圖書上刻畫 , 看看羅馬的細節 。
part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我給你們看這些的部分原因是 , 它有助於說明我所經歷的這個過程 , 試圖找出我對羅馬的感覺 , 以及我為何感受到它 。

a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的整體方式 , 還包括一系列的層次 。

but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但 , 把它們想成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一層水平層 , 垂直層層 , 垂直層層次 , 我心想 , 光是從頁面上剝下 , 就可以讓我用我剛才提到的來思考 , 如果我用正確的方式來說明 , 羅馬可以給你們看深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	在羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁上塗滿了傷疤 ; 幾世紀以來這些結構一直被改造而不是被摧毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊畫一個摺疊頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你就會看到它背後我的意思是傷疤組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小小的窗戶變得很重要 , 因為壞人要來了或其他的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應力全都被埋在管子底下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以剝出這一頁的palazzzo , 讓大家看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我還可以向各位展示 , 其中一個偉大的建築物的角落 , 上面有所有的巨大石塊 , 或是用磚塊和石頭做成的假石塊 , 比較常見的情況 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得稍微立體一點 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹窄的小街道 , 進入其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 只要用一個雙面大門的摺疊頁 , 如果你像我一樣在小時候讀一本彈出式書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭部的頁面包裹起來 , 是在那個廣場上 , 為了那短暫的時間 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我並沒有做任何比摺疊頁更複雜的事 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但後來我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神廟和前面的巴薩德拉•羅頓達 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不打開整本書 , 如果我只打開它90度 , 我們就在萬神殿的正面向下看 , 我們在看正頂端 , 或多或少在廣場上 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我用另一種方式把書轉過來 , 我們就在萬神廟前方的正方 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺紙 , 沒有把戲 , 只是一本不完全打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有前景 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 甚至可以把整本摺紙和唯一一部分的書結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以我們進入萬神殿 , 它生長等等 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它有點失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你試著讓大家注意一本書 , 一路上收集資訊 , 總是一件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 把我當作捕捉的標題
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是恐怖的鴿子 , 會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德修 。 」
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題可行 , 使用它 。 但它會是一段旅程 , 經過羅馬 , 展現出所有我喜歡羅馬的事 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一個坐在教堂頂上的鴿子
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天出門 , 做一些正常的鴿子 。 回來 , 整個地方被鷹架和綠色網子包覆著 , 這隻鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須找到另一個居住的地方 , 這讓我可以透過我最喜歡的目錄 , 我們從高層開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家族成員住在一起 ; 這不一定是件好事 , 但牠的確讓鴿子再度聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該以某種方式參與 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方 , 讓他們有危險的地方 , 他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學會幫他做把戲 , 用午餐時間來娛樂他 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出一個真實的鍵結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時病得很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他被教導他們拼他的名字 , 也就是艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	有一天他們在三四天看不見他 , 他住在這個小garret , 他們把他的名字拼起來 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量一起爬上了樓頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 一隻 la紅氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 帶著他到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘記提到這點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那只鴿子帶到城牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在舊羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋葬在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很歡呼的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長一段路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	所以 , 總之 , 我經歷了...再說一次 , 如果包裝沒有效果 , 如果故事沒有到哪裡去 , 我只想出標題 , 希望標題有點像把我踢向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它的確夠專注我 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁面 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是標題頁面 , 最終引領我找到解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在木鴿的外面傳遞訊息 , 她住在羅馬城外的牆壁 , 來到城市裡的某個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子就在阿比亞的上空飛行 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墓碑和松果等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它變得必要 , 且有可能 , 試著傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 而不會真的移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	越過塞斯提烏斯金字塔--這些在你看來很熟悉 , 即使你最近還沒去過羅馬渡過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的東西 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件最令人敬佩的鴿子做不到的事:它採用了一條很短的路線 , 這是我覺得必要的裝置 , 可以將這本書延伸到四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著羅馬競技場 , 穿越了聖母堂 , 位在哥斯穆德的聖母堂 , 以及海克力士的神廟 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎與米開朗基羅設計的palazzofarnese碰撞 , 由羅馬競技場狹窄逃離而建造的石頭 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯衝著柬埔寨德菲奧里島 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給我的學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完全的全然否定任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我覺得唯一重要的觀點規則就是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你就已經成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出這些消失點在哪裡 ; 一對夫妻在火星上 , 另一對在克雷蒙納州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但是進入廣場在聖母堂前面的廣場上 , 一場足球賽正在進行中 , 我們被球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球撞擊的糟糕插圖 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:這裡有聖母瑪莉亞•迪拉斯的腳步 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥的翅膀沒有發生 , 所以我必須重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看聖母瑪莉亞.德拉的步調 , 這些書很靈活 , 非常有互動性 , 只要把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到衝擊在紅線中捕捉到 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鳥兒在中世紀的大樓上將自己拉近了 , 剩下的中世紀塔塔之一 , 朝向桑格尼斯的教堂前進 , 向下看 , 向下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 往下看 , 再飛了幾次 ; 這是柏尼聖母神堂的雕像之一 , 接著 , 經過了美妙的布洛米尼聖母堂 , 在萬神殿直徑26英尺的地方 , 停下來 , 停下來 , 停留在萬神殿堂的距離 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面不斷翻轉 , 因為我們在飛翔 , 我們不用擔心地心引力在這個特別的時刻 , 所以這張圖可以在頁面上以任何方式被定位 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會得到一個令人興奮的結果 , 這並不讓人意外地用這種方式模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去美好的牆上佈滿了我剛才提到的混合物 ; 美麗的雕刻被放到《暴風雨》上方的牆上 , 標誌之類的 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到了palazzo的庭院 , 也就是我們的目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的一扇小窗 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把訊息從鳥的腿上移除 ; 這是它說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看畫板時 , 我們看到他正在做的是 , 事實上 , 一幅鴿子剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線延伸到所有的景象 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究者skylarstibbits在自行組裝上運作的概念是與其打造一些東西 , 而不是建立自我組裝的材料 , 很多dna組合的方式 。 這是早期的一個大概念 ; tibbits告訴我們三個棘手項目 , 暗示了自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylarstibbits:我們能做出製造自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向大家展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信很快我們的建築和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給你們看我所相信的 , 是目前的製造狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態中 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 50萬到100萬個部分 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的科技 , 在鋼鐵、水泥、玻璃中 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有振奮人心的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--[組裝時間] , 250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒內摺疊 , 或三十億個鹼基對中的dna , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統中有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率遠高於
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎無法犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以自我修復長壽
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 天然系統有著超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它轉化為我們的建設環境 , 那麼我們建造東西的方式有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將這簡單的序列解碼 , 基本上就是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可程式化的零件 , 可以用它來摺疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 讓它可以活化 , 讓我們的部分能夠從這個程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正冗餘 , 來保證我們已經成功地建構出我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要向你們展示一些項目我的同事和麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是宏觀機器人和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目是大規模可重組的機器人8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們被機械裝置、感應器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將想要摺疊的內容解碼成一連串的負120 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或轉動 , 然後你將這個序列傳送出去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位會收到負120個訊息 , 轉到那個單位 , 看看它是否到達這個地點 , 然後傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師 , 都致力於這個專案 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的帶到光線上去:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 幾千美元 , 很多男人小時製造這個八英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以把這個規模擴大嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人嵌入每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並且檢視被動的天性 , 或被動地嘗試進行重新配置程式 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它是最基本的計算方塊 , 也就是數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nandgate
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是大門會做計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 如同你正在建造你的磚塊 ,
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從前一個被放置的磚塊
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始插入他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它之前的做法 , 以及你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於0輸出 , 就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1的輸出 , 會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們擁有所有被建構出來的資訊 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	那就表示我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我複製 , 因為你的結構包含了確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一個部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入在告訴大家如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	這樣你就可以有東西爬上去 , 讀它 , 可以一比一的輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有任何外來的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以我要展示的最後一個專案 , 叫做偏移鏈 , 它可能是我們目前最激動的自我組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組和程式 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 它們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想要向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每一個單位是否該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編寫的結構 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體在旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你基本上可以在任何立體的形狀或一維的 , 二維的形狀完全被動地進入這個鏈子裡 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們 , 未來是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 它告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築、機器的新可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的程式性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那你就有了計算的新可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器、所有磚頭都能夠實際運算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以對此感到興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些計畫只是朝這個未來邁進的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自我組合世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登上了月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底兩次的最深處 。 下一代還剩下什麼去探索 ? 生物學家和探險家內森•沃夫斯建議這個答案:幾乎每樣東西 。 然後我們可以開始 , 他說 , 在這個不可見的小世界裡 ,
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃夫:剩下什麼要去探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀20世紀偉大的探險家roychapmanandrews
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , 安德魯斯帶領一系列的探險 , 前往未知的地區 , 像是在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很像人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來被說是印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給了一群中學學生一堂公開講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡要告訴各位 , 如果有任何事比在ted這裡演講更令人畏懼的話 , 它會試著把一群十二歲的孩子的注意力留在一個四十五分鐘的講課上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在講課結束時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個問題一直困擾著我 。
