there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想 , 我們當中許多人認為地球上偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 對於下一代 , 他們將要前往外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能找到重要的東西來探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們在地球上探索剩下的真的沒有意義嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他的做法是從菸草植物中取出感染的汁液 , 他會透過越來越小的過濾器來過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達那個時點 , 感覺到一定有比當時最小型的生命形式還要小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘媒介想出了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為病毒拉丁文為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們打開了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒組成了我們星球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式生命的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然的 , 這種世界的實用應用非常重大 , 像是天花的消滅 , 一種對子宮頸癌的疫苗出現 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這並不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們有了汽車 , 但我們對生命的形式一無所知 , 組成了我們星球上大部分的基因信息 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未見的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們能做到的不只是跳過表面 , 還能從某個特定物種的個別基因組來檢視 , 而是去檢視整個爆炸物 , 包含微生物的社群 , 在我們身邊 , 以及記錄這些物種的所有基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技巧應用到從土壤到皮膚 , 以及中間的所有東西 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在做這件事 , 定期的基礎是找出造成疫情爆發的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取下一個鼻腔 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 用來尋找呼吸道病毒 , 如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到許多人類遺傳信息的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分是來自你鼻子裡完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了非常非常驚人的景象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子中大約有20%的基因信息並不符合任何我們以前看過的任何東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際研究這類資料的小團體 , 其實我們當中有一些人開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前見過的東西 , 而是相當於一個未知的大陸在我們自己的基因信息中 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較不理想的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質不能被分類 , 也不能和我們以前見過的任何東西打字或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對很新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但隨著它們變得越來越準確 , 我們已經判斷出這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 或至少有一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 只存在於嬰兒期 , 有非常令人興奮的可能性存在:埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 正如尚未發現的生命跡象一樣 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們在探究一連串a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命型態 , 像是北京 , 會從根本上改變我們對生物的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這或許可以讓我們找出癌症的成因 , 來衝突我們 , 或是找出爆發時我們不熟悉的爆發源頭 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們一起 , 我們正開始一個倡議 , 探索生物暗物質 , 為新型態的生命存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們對病毒一無所知 , 生命型態構成了我們星球上大部分的基因信息 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆 , 我們可能完全沒有意識到新的人生階級在我們的鼻子下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代的探險家們提供了重要的一課:像威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特那樣的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想 , 如果我們把這一課說出來 , 應該是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為有完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追尋任何你選擇探索的領域裡的黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊都有未知 , 他們只是等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家大衛•德茲赫把理論物理放在後埋的火柴上 , 用來討論一個更急迫的物質:我們這個物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	我們在宇宙中的位置大衛.德瑞西斯
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這樣做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 大部分的歷史都已知 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其他東西 , 都是獨一無二的適合用來維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像它過去的思維和我們現在的存在一樣 , 最重要的是 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這個想法就是太空船以外的空間 , 宇宙是充滿敵意的 , 內部是我們所有的 , 我們所仰賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有別的機會了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都知道的事 , 和人類大部份的歷史所相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金說過的 , 我們只是一個典型行星表面的化學污垢 , 它繞著一個典型的恆星在軌道上 , 它位在一個典型的銀河系的外圍 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的這兩件事當中的第一件事就是說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合等等 , 第二個是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是 , 如果你認為這兩個是深層的真理 , 可以靠它來活下去 , 並告知你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎和彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能防止他們完全虛假 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們來看看四周 , 隨機朝向一個方向看 , 我們看到一面牆 , 還有一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要往同一方向走幾百英里 , 往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆壁或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 以及恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星在星系中來來 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 幾乎沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再更進一步 , 直到我們在銀河外面 , 回頭看 , 沒錯 , 這裡有巨大的銀河系 , 前面有螺旋形手臂 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時我們已經距離這裡10萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們在宇宙中的典型地點 , 到處都還沒有 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你必須到達星系間空間的一千倍之多 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	所以這是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的代價上 , ted已經安排了高解析度的浸泡在星際空間中的虛擬實境中 , 將來自星系間空間的景象呈現出來 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 請把燈關掉 , 這樣我們就可以看見了嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	不太完美 , 你可以看到 , 在星系間空間中是完全黑暗的 , 音高是暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著最近的恆星 , 而那顆恆星正以超級新星爆炸 , 而當你在它的光線接觸到你時 , 你仍然無法看見它的光芒 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙有多大、有多黑暗
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的明亮 , 如此聰明 , 以致於你在幾光年之內死去了 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也非常冷 , 低於絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常空洞 。 真空量比地球上最好的科技所能創造的真空量少了一百萬倍 。 所以這就是一個典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能讓燈光回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道這麼遙遠的環境 , 又如此不同 , 如此外星人 , 從任何我們習以為常的環境中得知 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這是什麼意思 ? 嗯 , 比我們從這裡更進一步--我是說 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 quasars 」 。 quasars原本的意思是 「 和平的物體 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著看起來有點像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是幾十億年前 , 而在數十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量的黑洞倒塌 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場導向了重力崩塌的一些能量 。 有些物質 , 以極大的噴射流的形式呈現 , 以極大的葉門照亮了葉子的光輝 , 以我認為是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理現象幾乎不像噴射流的物理現象 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法即時存活 。 語言在試圖描述其中一個噴射流中會是怎樣的情況時 , 會是如何 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像在經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在點燃場 , 數百萬年來 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個噴射流發生的方式正是數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 有些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 以及模型 , 然後預測 , 並且解釋 , 在現實中 , 最重要的是你的參考資料 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含一個精確的運作模式 , 一個方塊 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的一個超級形象 , 雖然它也包含了這個形象 , 而是一個解釋性的模型 , 體現出相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 一個結構的忠實與時間的增長有關 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特殊性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體的物體 , 不像彼此一樣 , 可能永遠無法體現出相同的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間 , 越來越多地在做 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷增加的精確度 , 萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中其他地方 , 它的結構性和因果性是整個物理現實的結構性和因果性 。 因此 , 遠遠不止是微不足道 , 物理定律允許這一切發生的事實 , 或甚至是強制實現這一切 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境是如何形成這種與宇宙其他地方的特殊關係呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金的評論有一點是真的 , 這是真的 , 但它是錯誤的強調 。 其中一點是 , 它的確是真的 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理學去做 。 沒有特殊的解讀 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用了我們在這裡所擁有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的成長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦--根本不知道製造電腦的方法 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較沒有實際性 , 但對於開放式的知識和解釋而言 , 同樣重要 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境被證據給淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好在300年前就開始進行測試 , 比如牛頓的地心引力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去所做的證據 , 早在數十億年前就在地球上掉下來了 , 幾十億年後 , 還會持續下跌數十億年 。 其他科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本的真理的證據只是為了我們星球的實現而已 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點飽和證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間空間中 , 這三種開放式創造知識的前提是最低的可能供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 ; 外面是漆黑的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實這只是另一個狹隘的錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間空間的立方體 , 和我們的家一樣大 , 太陽系 。 現在那個立方體是人為的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造 , 比如說一個自我控制的太空站 , 有一群科學家致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 超越目前的技術 , 甚至可以從星系間空間收集氫氣 , 將之形塑成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個無法理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可能可以避免我們去做 , 除了知道如何做之外 , 其他的也無法被禁止 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉換是核融合反應爐和證據呢 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	同樣的 , 人類感官也是暗的 。 但你只需要用望遠鏡 , 即使是現代設計的一個 , 向外看 , 你會看到我們從這裡看到相同的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能夠看到星星 , 和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠進行天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最困難的科學是生物學領域之旅 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生命之星 , 回到最近的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴你 , 抱歉 , 理查 , 但我從來沒有像生物學領域旅行那麼多 , 我想我們每隔幾億年就可以完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了所有開放式知識的前提 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中任何一個地方 , 都可能成為我們所處的相同的樞紐 , 如果我們知道如何去做的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是在一個獨一無二的可居住地 ,
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠開放解釋的話 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 地球也是一樣 。 受污染的地球也是 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源充沛 , 但知識卻稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以知識為基礎的宇宙觀或許我認為應該要讓我們感到非常特別 。 但這也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有有需要的具體知識 , 能夠生存下去的宇宙挑戰 , 我們就無法生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超級新星在幾光年之外 , 我們都會死定了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁里斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模殺傷性武器來恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機會能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在會議中談到這點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我確實認同他這件事 , 我們可以生存 , 而且我們也無法存活 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否能及時創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	前所未有的危險 。 物種經常滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終止了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有曾經存在過的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外 , 那麼邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是使用一種特徵來區別我們的物種 , 以及我們的文明 , 來自所有其他人的名字 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	現在讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是為了說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是全球暖化的正確物理學家 。 我只是一名layman 。 對於層級來說 , 理性的事情是認真看待主導的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 實在太遲了 , 無法避免一場災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果我們目前最好的選擇是防止二氧化碳排放 , 像京都議定書 , 和經濟活動的限制 , 以及數千億美金或其它的巨大成本 , 那麼這已經是任何合理的衡量方法所造成的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡導者的行動甚至還沒有解決問題 , 只需要稍微把問題做後事 。 所以太遲才會避開它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 以至任何人意識到危險之前 , 都無法避免它 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放即將在數十億人會死亡的新冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這堂課對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能一直知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以低於災難本身的成本來解決 , 那麼就不會有太多的爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 而不只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的治療 , 但只有我們知道要預防什麼才行 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你曾被打鼻子 , 那麼醫學的科學並不能教你如何避開拳擊 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也幾乎不會達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前這個世界正隨著計劃著降低氣體排放 , 以各種成本 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要和計畫減低溫度 , 計畫要活在更高的溫度下 , 不計一切代價 , 有效率又便宜 。 有些計畫是存在的 , 像是太空中的一群鏡子 , 將太陽光反射開來 , 鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 或是一般來說的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	面對我們還沒意識到的問題 , 不要無窮盡地避開我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板 , 然後在上面刻畫 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中之一是: 「 問題很容易解決 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一幅畫: 「 問題是必然的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何能脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅•羅默揭示了一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 , 城市規模的管理區 , 由一個國家的聯盟統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅馬的激進想法:特許城市 。
take a look at this picture .	請看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的路燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒遇過這些特別的學生 , 但我遇過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色襯衫裡的那位
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我會賭nelson有一個手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以這個謎題是
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼nelson可以接觸到尖端科技 , 像是手機 , 但沒有一百歲的科技 , 可以在家中產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 換句話說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不好的規則可以預防這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人取得 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 這條規則是說 , 它必須以很低、很低的價格銷售電力 , 事實上 , 價格很低 , 價格很低 , 它會損失在它銷售的每一個單位上 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既不是資源 , 也不是激勵機制 , 要吸收許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到有一套不同的規則 , 企業賺取小利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機要簽署更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	那是nelson從底下購買他的電話的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過那些規則如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變收購電力的規則 , 但卻跑進了商業和消費者的抗爭中 , 他們想要保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他陷入了規則 , 避免他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而nelson則被困在街燈下研究 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能為改變規則發展出一些規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想爭辯的是 , 有一個普遍的抽象的見解 , 我們能做出實用的見解 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給更多人選擇 , 以及更多的領導人選擇 , 在許多國家 , 他們也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現這兩者之間的對立是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導人的那種選擇 , 像是給予總統在電力上提高價格的選擇 , 奪走經濟上人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇能夠繼續消費補充的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方法 , 那會給我們一組改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelson也能上網
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則所造成的傷害影響 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看太空總署在夜間拍攝的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別檢查亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 在這裡 , 這就像是黑洞 , 和它的鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	你不會驚訝地發現 , 北韓的規則會讓人們在黑暗中保持住 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但重要的是要意識到北韓和南韓始於一系列的規則 , 不論法律和法規都一樣 , 在更深層的理解、規範、文化、價值觀 , 和信念上都一樣 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致他們一組的規則非常不同的路徑 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以我們可以改變 , 我們人類可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 做得更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡有線 ,
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 相較之下這裡的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國大約有相同數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各有一半的居民是海地或多明尼加共和國
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則可能會很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不僅僅是規則不好 , 因為政府太強勢和壓迫 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要用良好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能只撕下 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法來建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國大大展示了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料的一開始 , 中國是全世界的高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人有先驅的科技 , 像是鋼、印刷、槍械 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵那些想法的傳播──一種利潤動機──可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	很快的 , 他們採用的規則讓創新慢下來 , 把中國從世界其他地方切斷 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展出更新的規則 , 中國人從這些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入停滯不前 , 在世界其他地方放大 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪了中國平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到大約是百分之三 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代後期 , 有些事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的經濟開始起飛 , 中國開始迅速趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 你可以得到一個線索 , 提示這個過程會導致中國的規則大大改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的地點 , 這裡是線的邊緣 , 是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時間 , 運作在非常不同的規則之下 , 比起當時從事市場經濟工作的其他國家 , 中國的規則 , 和當時由英國人管理的非常不一樣 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 到像是縫紉襯衫、製作玩具等工作的地方 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 若要取得收入增加的過程 , 技能會造成非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	「 香港 」 也是 「 鄧小平的領導人 」 能複製的模式 , 當他們決定將所有大陸都移向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們採用的只是創造一些特殊區塊 , 某種意義上 , 可以做到的 , 英國所做的是:讓有機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要在裡面選項的人參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍創造了四個特殊的經濟區:中國可以來這裡工作的區塊 , 都市長得很快 ; 還有外國公司可以進來做事的區塊 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個城市叫深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一家台台灣公司 , 製作了在座許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用來自中國人的勞工搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸風箏在同樣的意義上開放 , 最後在這些地方展示了成功 , 人們可以選擇進去 , 因為他們提供的優勢 , 圍住了 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡展現了成功 , 達成了共識 , 朝向整個經濟的市場模式邁進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子告訴我們好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:保存人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的尺度上運作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村莊的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但一個村莊會太小 , 無法取得你能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在良好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你嘗試改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會來持久 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人往前放 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市讓你有機會創造新的地方 , 有人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而它們夠大到可以得到所有好處當我們數百萬人在良好的規則下一起工作
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是我們設想一個叫做特許城市的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則開始 , 把所有需要的規則都明確地吸引到需要建立城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者來建立基礎建設--電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 誰會先來僱用那些搬遷到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而且你需要吸引家庭 , 那些會來到那裡的居民 , 永久住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那個憲章 , 人們就會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中捕捉到的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們允許在未居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領土開始
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以住在新憲章下面 , 但沒有人被迫住在下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是領導人的選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導人的那種選擇我們必須允許國與國之間的合作潛力:國與國之間的合作情況 , 實際上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 先建立一個小小的市場模式 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 無意間 , 透過香港的行動 , 將世界貧窮減少得比上個世紀所有援助計畫所做的還多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這種合作關係再次複製 , 我們就能得到這樣的好處 , 遍及全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會涉及到責任的授權 , 一個從一個國家到另一個國家的授權 , 來接管某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這樣說的時候 , 你們有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 可以讓我們往後退 , 可以停止 , 可以讓我們的能力 , 和我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的壞處在於 , 我們的一些援助計劃中是不好的 , 是因為它涉及了強制力和執行力的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇 , 不論是為了領導者 , 還是為了那些將居住在這些新地方的人民 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 , 選擇是對戰鬥和爭執的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談如何實踐它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	以一個特定的領導人raulcastro為例他是古巴的領導人
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚曾想過 , 他有機會為古巴做點事 , 像是鄧小平為中國做了什麼 , 但他在古巴沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他在南部有一點點光 , 那裡有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣附近有一個區塊 , 在那裡 , 一條條約給美國一塊土地負起一塊塊地的責任 , 比曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚走向加拿大總理 , 說: 「 聽著 , 雅典人有個可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要出來 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為何你不 , 加拿大呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造經營一個特別的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新城市在上面建設
allow many people to come in .	允許許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會緊緊抓住 。 但這將會是通往現代經濟和現代世界的通往我的國家的通道 。 "
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模型還能在哪裡被試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	其中許多人完全拿到一個人們可以選擇的特區的概念 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	改變規則的規則
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是創造新規則的一種方式 , 讓大家不用強迫 , 不用強迫 , 就會讓民眾反對 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有信賴的承諾 , 投資者會來建立港口 , 建立道路 , 在一個新城市中 , 他們可以做出更有信賴的承諾 , 如果他們和一個夥伴國家一起做的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在一些安排上 , 這有點像escrow的帳號 , 在那裡 , 你將土地放在escrow的帳號中 , 而伴侶的國家負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多的土地 , 在那裡 , 新城市可以建造 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這片土地有著巨大的延伸 , 數億人可以住的地方 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納一下 , 不只一、二個特許城市 , 還有數十個城市 , 能夠為數億人創造出地方 , 也許未來世紀會有數十億人移居到城市 , 對他們來說 , 有足夠的土地嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們晚上看著燈光 , 有一件事誤導了 , 那就是 , 視覺上 , 大部分的世界都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我向各位展示為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這所有土地的代表為例
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個代表地球上所有可耕地的方塊 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被三十億人口居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到矩形的底部 , 你可以看到現有30億居民的城市只佔了地球上可耕地的3% 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	如果我們想要為十億人建造城市 , 他們會是這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從可耕地的3%降到4%
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大幅降低地球上的人類足跡 , 做法是建造更多人們可以搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所統治 , 它們可以成為人們從犯罪、疾病和不良衛生的城市 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	可以得到像電力這樣的基本功用
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特區城市 , 我們要怎麼做才能再建造出更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	要有一本手冊是有幫助的
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授可以做的是寫一些可能進入這本手冊的細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們經營城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考像這樣的問題 , 假設它不只是加拿大和拉爾•卡斯楚處理的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	巴西也可能是參與者 , 西班牙也一樣 。 也許古巴也想成為四向聯合創業的夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	前例較少 , 但那很容易解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這個 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港都是在他們開始時所擁有的土地上的巨大收穫 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用土地的價值來支付像警察、法庭等東西 , 但學校系統和醫療系統 , 這也讓這個地方更吸引人居住 , 讓這個地方有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這個區域的人的誘因 , 並建立起基本規則 , 朝向正確的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以 , 還有許多其他類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能讓低成本、負擔得起的建築物在第一份工作中工作的人 , 組裝成像iphone一樣的東西 , 但讓那些建築物能有效率 , 並且確保它們是安全的 , 這樣它們不會在地震或颶風中跌倒 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節是可以解決的 , 但那些已經開始追求這些東西的人 , 都可以知道 , 沒有路障 , 沒有任何障礙 , 除了想像力的失敗之外 , 它能讓我們不受全球性的雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能這麼好 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現它們時 , 他們就會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀少的物品 , 共享意味著我們每人都得到較少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類的想法:規則管理我們如何和彼此互動的規則 ; 規則像是 , 讓我們有稅制系統來支援一所研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在政府辦公室註冊土地的所有權 , 人們可以以 「 獨立 」 的承諾 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新我們的規則 , 特別是在思考改變規則的規則 , 這樣我們就不會陷入不良的規則 , 那麼我們就能繼續前進 , 真正地讓世界變得更好 , 這樣像尼爾森和他的朋友就不用再在街燈下研究了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先鋒克萊格•凡特從他史詩般的探險中休息一會兒 , 來談談他的團隊發現的數以百萬計的基因 , 來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對於衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者非常超越悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我的18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位的是我們要如何從讀取基因編碼轉換到最初開始寫代碼的階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前 , 我們這個月發表了第一個免費的有機體的序列 , 內容是哈莫斐斯的流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月的時間 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用2到8小時的順序進行同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 大量的基因組被加入:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	從10多年前開始的這個階段來看基因組學 , 到今年年底 , 我們可能有3到5個基因組測序 ; 這是數百個基因組測序 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會取得一項資金 , 到定序今年130個基因組 , 作為環保有機體的副計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的速度改變了
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎無法在這個星球上抓住表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分的人不會意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物組成地球生物量約一半 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物量的1/1 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津人不太常做的事 , 但如果你能把它送到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 記住每一毫升的細菌就有大約一百萬隻細菌 , 依照一千萬隻病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	只有不到5000種微生物種類在兩年前就有了特徵 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了sorceri二次探險 , 我們在那兒 , 正如海洋探險一樣 , 試圖每200英哩採集一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們開始在百慕達進行我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到海利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸、加勒比海、巴拿馬運河 , 再到達加拉巴哥群島 , 然後橫跨太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫跨印度洋的路上 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的責任 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分原因是要協助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要將海水過濾過濾 , 然後在不同的濾鏡上收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以每24小時完成一億個基因編碼的序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們有了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 被認為是我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一、兩種有機體有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有在海洋上部的物種都在溫暖的區域 , 都有相同的感光器 , 並使用陽光作為它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因 , 以及五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這點延伸到空氣中 , 帶著史隆基金會的獎金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或關閉禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們每天收集十億微生物的次數 , 來自紐約市的一棟大樓上 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在正處於定序所有這些的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	僅僅在資料收集方面 , 就在加拉巴哥群島 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們會在海洋中的樣本中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	以不同溫度梯度來看 , 有些是合乎邏輯的 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據溫度紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水的樣本有極大的差異 , 就豐富的物種來說 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令我們驚訝的事是這些攝影機偵測到不同的光波長 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些巨大的變化 , 從地區到地區 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海中 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 感光受器往往會看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化可能更大 , 可能在極端的紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了試著去評估我們的基因到底是什麼 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們在遠征途中 , 所有的資料 , 代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共約2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著將這些放入基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但我們在環境中採用的每一個新樣本 , 加上這些新家庭的線性流動 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處在這個星球上最早發現的基礎基因、組件和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們和動物在右上角 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物集合在一起 , 我們大概只有不到三萬個 , 可能還有十幾千個不同的基因家族 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我覺得這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計元件
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	而我們以基因中心的角度來看 , 或許回到理查德•達金斯的想法 , 而不是以基因為中心的角度來看 , 這些基因組成的構造是不同的 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna、合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年或二十年間 , 已經改變了dna定序的步調 , 變得非常快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們第一次想到合成基因組學 , 是在1995年我們將第二組基因定序後的1995年 , 也是從菌根生殖器中得來的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我把生殖器關掉 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有一千八百個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有一組更小的基因 , 可能會產生一個最小的作業系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做轉子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉接器只是基因密碼中隨機插入的小片段 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會瓦解其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一個可以取代變形蟲插入的基因的地圖 , 我們稱之為 「 無傷大的基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能依據環境中到底是什麼來定義一個本質或非本質的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著將13種相關生物的基因組和基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因 , 共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 就會膨脹得更大 , 當我們研究核心基因時 , 大約310左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 取決於你對此的看法 , 大約300到400個基因 , 來自500個最小 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是建立一個人工染色體 , 裡面有那些基因 , 我們必須在以鑄造為基礎的時尚中做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片中合成精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事研發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們合成一個50000個鹼基對的病毒 , 在僅僅兩週的時間內 , 準確度是100% , 以它的序列和生物學而言 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人振奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna片段注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的生產 , 轉過頭 , 然後殺死了細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這並不是第一種合成病毒──小兒麻痺病毒一年前就被製造出來了──但它只有十分之一的活躍性 , 且花了三年的時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174結構的漫畫
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這個案例是軟體現在建立自己的硬體 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關心生物戰事 , 而我最近在參議院委員會舉辦的證人 , 以及一個特別的委員會 , 美國政府設立了重新審視這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為很重要的是要記住現實 , 與人們的想像力會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已被定序的病毒都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉或天花感到害怕 , 但這個生物的dna不具傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	安全部門真正擔心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 致力於創造生物戰事代理人 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被打亂了 , 未來要製造設計病毒的知識份子應該少很多 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為單細胞有機體在兩年內就有可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	很有可能 , 真正的細胞 , 是我們擁有的 , 在十年內就可以做到的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在做數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以把鑄模和基因轉換成這個人造染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 如何把所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組的系統 , 將它們重新組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinococcusradiodurans , 可以採用三百萬個放射線 , 不被殺害 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆炸後的基因體在12到24小時內重新組合 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這個有機體在地球上普遍存在 , 可能因為我們的旅遊而存在外太空 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一個玻璃製造器經過了大約50萬次輻射後
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒、裂縫 , 同時坐在底部的微生物變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張圖表顯示一百七十萬次輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的被炸開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些有機體真的很驚人 , 我們可能有上千種 , 在這星球上有上萬種不同的物種 , 能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是把它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了環保和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們測序的第三個生物中 , 甲烷ocococacsjannaschii-它住在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 而它的碳來自於環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 現在住在二氧化碳中 , 可以捕捉到它 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 我們不用從石油中吸取碳來做合成過程 , 我們有機會從大氣中捕捉碳 , 將之轉換為生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 住在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來減少水分 , 來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有數種途徑 , 可以被工程化代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一項主要的計畫 , 有了挪威的現狀 , 用來捕捉並將天然氣場中的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我想將有一個新領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人一天製造或許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有的生物學 , 透過篩選 , 不論是篩選氫氣生產 , 或是化學生產 , 或僅僅可行 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因扮演的角色 , 就會很好的接觸到它 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 從陽光直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們認為有一種氧氣敏感的氫氣 , 會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維素 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖和發酵的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中 , 產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	製藥生產已經在使用微生物的主要實驗室裡了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物的化學成分 , 比我們最好的化學家所能產生的更複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來工程的物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救 , 也可能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年開始了實驗 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來評估我們是否應該嘗試製造人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各式各樣的宗教領袖都把他們的劇本當成法律書籍 , 他們無法在當中找到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以這一定是沒問題的 。 唯一的最終考量就是生物戰事方面 , 但給了我們 , 讓我們開始做這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛資助一個多元制度的研究 , 想找出對社會的風險和利益是什麼 , 以及像我自己的科學團隊應該要在這個領域使用的規則 , 我們試著在前進的同時設定好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們是否能夠設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 或許可以革命發展中國家可以做什麽 , 並透過各種簡單的過程提供什麼 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說幸福和成功是根植在一個我們多數人不認同的特質:我們對過去、現在、未來的方向 。 他建議我們在時間上校正我們的外觀 , 作為改善我們生活的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦津巴多開立一個健康的時段
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些想法 , 關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好了 , 開始時鐘 。 30秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大概是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來試試在亞當的誘惑中對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 不要這麼想 , 吃點東西 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 咬一口 , 亞當 。 不要放棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口咬 , 什麼地獄 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生命是誘惑的 。 一切都是為了產量 , 抗拒 , 是的 , 不是的 , 後來的 , 衝動的 , 反思的 , 現在的焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會把獵物降到當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	少女承諾了性墮胎和處女論 , 直到婚前--謝謝妳布希--大多數--60% , 60% , 導致性誘惑在一年內發生 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有使用節育 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓我們誘惑四歲小孩 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來之前 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然會付出代價 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	結果是三分之二的孩子給予誘惑
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 。 當然 , 還有其他人 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 他們延遲了晚期 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	華特.密歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 回到14年後 , 試圖發現那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	反抗的孩子和反抗的孩子在很多方面都有很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抵抗分數高達250分的孩子們 ,
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 那就像是一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們很有自信 , 也很有決心 。 對我來說 , 關鍵在於 , 他們是將 「 未來 」 而非 「 展現出來 」 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間的觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間的觀點是研究個人、所有人 , 如何將你人類經驗的流動分割成時間區域或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	它們在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育程度之間有所不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是它們會變得有偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用它們 , 並低估了其他的使用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做出什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做了一個決定 , 你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在即時情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 以及你感覺到什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而這些人 , 當他們用這種形式做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現況 」 , 因為他們的焦點是現在的 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說: 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們會把這些人稱為 「 鬆散 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在 「 什麼 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是有關預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們的焦點在將來會變成什麼樣子 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想論 , 時間的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你完全不知道的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	也就是說 , 你有這些偏見的時間觀點的程度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種方式 。 有兩種方式可以呈現 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被遺忘 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面 , 或是負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 「 後世主義 」 , 即:你把焦點放在人生的喜悅上 , 或現在的流行主義者──它不重要 , 你的人生被控制著 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展心靈靈靈活性 , 轉換時間觀點 , 會流暢地看待情況的要求 , 那就是你要學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳的時間檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度的正面 。 高度的未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和在當下共產主義的主導 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	並且總是在負面和現代主義上低落 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合是你從過去的正面給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份 , 和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	你從未來得到的就是翅膀 , 來到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從當下的享樂主義得到的 , 是能量、探索自己、地方、人、感性 。
