any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過時的觀點都比正面積極多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲的是什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲有趣的時間 , 犧牲個人的侮辱
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們為了工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 與一些ted成員產生共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	對我來說 , 很有共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯區長大 , 一個住在過去和現在的西西西里亞家庭 , 每個人都住在過去 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來到這裡 , 是一個走過頂端的人 , 他做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等待你得到其中兩顆 , 直到我學會平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 「 現代主義 」 , 把焦點放在 「 正面 」 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以前更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 且我比以前更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正把這個應用到許多世界問題上:改變學校孩子的輟學率 , 結合成癮 , 增強青少年的健康 , 治癒從時間比喻中得到奇蹟般的抗爭 , 提高了奇蹟可以促進永續發展和保育 , 減少了實體的復健率 , 在那裡有50%的輟學率 , 改變了自殺式恐怖份子的訴求 , 改變家庭衝突 , 成為時間區域衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說:許多生命的謎題可以透過了解你的時間觀和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法是如此簡單 , 所以很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深奧 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	一百年後 , 現今的標題會有多少影響 ? 1000年後 ? kirkcitron的《漫長新聞》收集了今天重要的新聞 , 數十年後 , 甚至會有共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他點出了近期的頭條新聞標題 , 帶著我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 ,
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社每年就有三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長遠來看 , 那些故事當中有多少其實很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫由現在很長的基金會成立 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們正在尋找的新聞故事可能在五、一百、一萬年後至今仍至關重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過這個過濾器來看新聞時 , 很多事情都是由此而來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以a.p.去年的最高故事來說 , 在十年內這將很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那真是太酷了 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頂端故事是經濟 , 我打賭 , 不久後 , 這次的經濟衰退將會是舊新聞 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事可能會對未來造成改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 讓我們以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有一天如果你是一隻老鼠 , 就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近一些故事:奈米生物用真蜂毒液將基因送入大腦 ; 一個他們建造出來的機器人 , 可以在人體上爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那資源呢 ? 我們要如何養活九十億人呢 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們有六十億人在餵食 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不經基因改造作物 , 英國就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	很幸運地 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭上了十億人在[印度語]的研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得很不一樣 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 且他們可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經把美國當作世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經把德國壓抑成最大的出口國 , 他們開始對孩子們進行dna檢測 , 選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們發現各式各樣的方法來推回已知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:阿根廷有一個螞蟻蟻群 , 現在已經散佈到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎與我們無關 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年我為史上漫長新聞報導挑選的就是這個:在月球上找到水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群在上面放置得更容易 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡洛琳•波科展現圖像 , 從卡西尼號航行到土星 , 把焦點放在它最大的月球 , 泰坦星 , 以及冰凍土衛二上 , 這似乎是用來射擊冰流的噴射 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化 ,
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡洛琳•波可讓我們飛往土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我將帶大家踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這段旅程是你我已經踏上好多年了 , 50年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不但真的將腳踏在月球上 , 我們還在將機器人的太空船移到所有行星上 , 8顆行星上 , 我們已經登陸了小行星 , 還帶著彗星 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船正前往冥王星 , 前所知是一顆行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機器人的任務都是一個更大的人類旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解某件事 , 去了解我們宇宙之處 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球、地球、地球 , 以及我們 , 如何在上面生存 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 都有土星 。 我們曾到過土星 , 在1980年代早期我們造訪過土星之前 , 我們對土星的調查已經更加深入 , 自從卡西尼號太空船開始 , 穿越星際空間七年之久 , 在2004年夏天圍繞著土星的土星運行軌道 , 成為人類最早期人類建立的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞察力 , 且顯然超越了對比 , 這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙接觸 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張andromedanebula的美麗圖片 , 它是我們對銀河系最接近、最大型的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡有一塊美麗的旋渦星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程真的是一部分 , 也是人類旅程更大的比喻 , 來了解我們周遭事物的相互連結性 , 以及人類如何融入圖片中 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位我們用卡西尼號學過的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我不能給你們看我們過去兩年半拍攝的美麗照片 , 因為我就是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我將要集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事中從這個重大的探險探險中浮現出來我們正在圍繞著土星 , 過去兩年半的時間
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星伴隨著一個非常大且多樣化的月球 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸從幾公里大到全美各地都一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	我們所拍攝的土星大部分美麗的照片 , 其實 , 都是土星和它的衛星 , 這是土星 , 這是土星 , 土星是土星 , 這裡是土星 , 土星展示的是愛德森 , 展示了它們的垂直薄度 , 和月球土衛二一樣 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中有兩顆是立體的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 是太陽系中最大的一個未被探索的地形擴張 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體有很長的感動人士觀看了行星
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大又厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為更像地球上的環境 , 或至少在過去 , 比起太陽系中其他的身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層很大 , 就像你在這個房間裡呼吸的分子 , 只是它的大氣層被一些簡單的有機物質困擾 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷等 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	在泰坦的大氣層中 , 這些分子會被分解掉 , 它們的產品會結合在一起 , 製造出討厭的粒子 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種迷宮無所不在 , 完全是全球化和全面性的霸主 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也就是為什麼你不能用眼睛在看得見的光譜上看到表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 在我們到達卡西尼號之前 , 數十億年的時間 , 溫柔地移到水面上 , 並在厚厚的有機煙霧中覆蓋表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以就像泰坦一樣 , 泰坦等於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 特別是甲烷和乙烷 , 可能是土衛六地表溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要將水帶到地球上 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可凝聚的 , 因此意識到這種情況會帶到整個世界的奇異可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 沒錯 , 在這些雲之上 , 你有數百公里長的黑洞 , 防止任何陽光到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管很冷 , 土衛六的地表下雨仍然會下降 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 雨會做什麼 , 它會雕刻海溝 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和坑洞中游泳 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把水泥洗掉高山峰和山丘 , 降到低地上 。 停下來 , 一分鐘思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像泰坦的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上午跟地球上過渡的深地球一樣暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 很惡劣 , 很可能在下雨 , 你可能正站在密西根湖的岸邊 , 用油漆薄薄薄 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是在我們到達卡西尼號之前我們對土衛六表面的看法 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 雖然在細節上並不相同 , 但這故事的確是那麼的令人著迷的 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼號人一樣 , 一直都在冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有一層又厚又延伸的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是一張泰坦的照片 , 來自太陽的背景 , 背景是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	還有另一個月球 , 我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 這是個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們有卡西尼號的儀器 , 可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們也拍過這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮且黑暗的區域 , 這大約是目前為止對我們來說是如此 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在太神秘了:我們無法弄清楚我們在土衛六上看到的是什麼 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近看這個區域 , 你會開始看到像我們不知道的單頻道一樣的東西 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面卻很少 , 意思是說它是個非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	而有些特徵看起來是構造的 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來像被拉扯了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到某個星球上有任何線性的東西時 , 就意味著有一個裂痕 , 就像斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	因此 , 它已經在板塊上改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到 , 在我們進入軌道六個月之後 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人被視為卡西尼號探測泰坦的高光照 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號已經運行了七年 , 遍佈了太陽系 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩小時半的時間 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這是多麼重要的一件事 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系著陸 , 這是人類史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這實在太重大了 , 在我心中 , 這個事件應該要被讚頌在美國和歐洲各個城市的滴答帶遊行 , 令人遺憾的是 , 這並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是很重大的原因 。 這是國際化使命 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國被慶祝 , 以及在英文口音中被賦予的慶祝 , 還有美國口音 , 還有德文口音 , 還有法文和義大利文和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是關於 「 聯合國 」 這個詞的一個動人的示範 , 應該指的是:一個真正的聯合國 , 加入大規模的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 探索一個行星是非常大的必要之處 , 為了了解一個行星系統 , 對於人類歷史上所有人來說 , 已經是不可預測的了 , 而現在人類卻碰到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以那是--我是說 , 我只是在談這件事 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是一個極大的情緒事件 , 這是我個人永遠不會忘記的 , 你們也不該忘記的 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但不管怎樣 , 探測器在降落過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 同時也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器上看到土衛六表面的第一張照片是什麼感覺 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這是個令人震驚的 , 因為我們希望這些其他照片從軌道上拍下來 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是一種不明確的模式 , 一種地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	它是一種垂直排水模式 , 只能由液體的流動而形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟蹤這些頻道 , 可以看到它們是如何匯合的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	然後將它們匯集到這裡的通道 , 這條通往這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是一條海岸線
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里處拍攝的 , 好嗎 ? 同樣的 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是一個航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機飛越美國 , 你就會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼亞航空公司飛過泰坦航空的窗口 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在表面上休息 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 第一張從外太陽系的月球表面拍的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰卵石 , 對吧 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	下面的探測器基本上就是土衛六相當於一塊泥土 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一塊未溶解的地面 , 被液態甲烷給困擾著 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很有可能這種材料已經被清洗掉了土衛六的高地 , 透過我們所看到的這些管道 , 流動了數十億年 , 來填補低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 仍然沒有我們的影像中 , 或甚至惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們赤道地區的電影 , 展示了這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 被幾公里分開 , 再延長幾公里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有數百、高達一千或一百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會拿到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再次感到困惑:沒有液體的屍體 , 直到最後 , 我們在極地看到了湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在泰坦南極的一個湖泊場地 ,
it's about the size of lake ontario .	和安大略湖的大小差不多 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過了泰坦北極 , 再次發現 , 我們在這裡發現了一個特徵 , 跟卡斯皮亞海的大小一樣 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 看來 , 液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少在這個季節中 , 顯然是在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個很了不起、很神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它是外星人 , 但很奇怪的地球 , 也有類似地球的地質形成 , 和一個極大的地理多樣性 , 它是一個非常迷人的世界 , 它只能在太陽系中對複雜性和豐富性進行對比 , 而它本身就是地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小月 , 大約十分之一的土衛六大 。 你可以在這裡看到 , 在英格蘭旁邊 , 只為了向你展示大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二非常白 , 非常亮 , 它的表面很明顯地被破壞了 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現 , 我們發現在南極點 , 我們在看南極點 , 在這裡 , 我們找到了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 。 這些碎片覆蓋著有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個區域 , 南極區 , 溫度升高了 。 這是地球上最熱的地區 , 也是身體上最熱的地區 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就跟發現地球上的南極比熱帶一樣奇怪 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 當我們照了額外的圖片 , 我們發現從這些碎裂中 , 噴射出的噴射線是很好的 , 結冰粒子延伸了數百英里到太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張影像彩色編碼 , 帶出光線的層級時 , 我們看到這些噴射流進了土衛六上方幾千英里的空間 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊對這樣的影像進行了檢查 , 就像這張 , 思考了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴射流可能從土衛二表面下的液態水袋中噴發出來 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水、有機物質和過熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代星球探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合生命有機體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	而且我不認為我需要告訴你們在我們太陽系其他地方的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或是其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學的涵義 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明基因的發生不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 藉由推斷 , 整個宇宙和137億年的歷史發生了相當驚人的數量 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球是我們所知唯一仍有生命存在的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們唯一知道的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代發出警告和連貫性 , 我們會原諒你 , 如果你沒有 , 好吧 , 你會記得1968年阿波羅八號太空人拍的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中所處位置的感覺有著巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號首先拍了一張相同的照片 , 這是人類從來沒有見過的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全食 , 從土星的另一端看過 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可能美麗的圖片中 , 你可以看到太陽的主要光環 , 你可以看到太陽的折射圖像 , 你看到這個光環 , 事實上 , 由土衛二的表面所產生 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以在這個美麗的圖像中發現 , 我們自己的星球的景象 , 在土星光環的臂中擠滿 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有件深刻動人的事 , 就是從外太空看我們自己 , 並在其他世界的星球上捕捉到我們小藍色的星球 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 以及我們從中獲得的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這次探索旅程得到的最佳獎賞 , 是在半個世紀前開始的 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年時 , 全世界只有15%的人被繪製出來 。 這減緩了一場災難後的援助遞送 , 並隱藏了未使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 在這場演講中 , google的laliteshkatragadsa的地圖示圖示 , 一個利用全球各地人民繪製的地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	laliteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 塞隆納吉斯摧毀了緬甸人 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人並供應該地區
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路的地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有任何幫助來接觸周圍的受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 全世界只有15%的人被描繪成可編程的地理細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國開始著手解決世界上大部分人口普及的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但協助就要來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40名志工用了一個新軟體來繪製十二萬公里的道路、三千間醫院、物流及解脫點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項科技 , 賦予我們每個人在地圖上所知道的資訊 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這套軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地的企業 , 影像商店到街角的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名herandodesoto承認大部分開發中國家的經濟利益是將大量的未經考量的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	例如 , 僅僅在印度 , 數兆美元的房地產仍然沒有被考慮到 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家的數千名使用者就已經繪製了數百萬筆資訊 , 創造出了一幅從未思考過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切都是由熱情使用者到處都有的力量實現 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看看目前使用者製作的一些地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 正如我們所說 , 在170個國家 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑 , 剛剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	還有 , 離家近一點 , chalua , 班加羅爾的一個n.g路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學、手勢辨識的結果 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數千個用戶的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個用戶 , 一次編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們地球70%未開發的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 布德鲁斯村10個月的非暴力抗議停止跨越他們橄欖園的障礙 。 你聽過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西的電影製作人朱麗亞•巴查查亞問為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突的暴力 , 而不是在有一天可能帶來和平的非暴力領袖 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力事件
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平的手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 有一個問題總是在問:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花時間拍攝數十名巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 他們來自以色列士兵和移居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試圖鑄造一個龐大的國家非暴力運動來結束佔領並建立地區的和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 大部分的人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧在國外發生的事情和認知之間是其中一個關鍵原因 , 也是為什麼我們還沒有一個巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動已經成功的原因 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以 , 今天我來這裡是要談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 在西岸、加薩及其他地方──但今天 , 我的個案研究會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 要讓非暴力行為成長主要缺少的 , 不是要讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經是的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	允許我說明一下這一點 , 藉由帶你到這個叫做布德鲁斯村莊 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個分隔障礙 , 這個障礙的一部分會建在村落頂端 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並被包圍住 , 所以他們會失去西岸其他地方的自由權 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導 , 他們發起了一場和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這一切發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 所以你們對於實際在地面上的樣子有一種感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知牆將與以色列分離巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們意識到牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:圍籬其實有解決方案來恐怖 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男子:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被以色列兄弟姐妹加入了數十位 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列激進分子:沒有什麼比非暴力反對軍隊更害怕的了 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試著推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須把我們對傳統思維的空虛
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們處於完全和諧狀態 , 我們想要把它散播到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	爭執:一個聯合國
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和流行的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:圍籬的衝突持續 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去散播人群 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是現場子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	像是furujah , 到處射擊
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列激進分子:我確信我們都會死去 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有一些人 , 甚至沒有在牛 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	我們辦得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體無法報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 在2003年發生的不平凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民在十個月的和平抗爭後 , 說服了以色列政府 , 將圍牆的路線移離他們的土地和綠線 , 也就是國際認可了以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭從此蔓延到西岸和耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦鄰里 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體大多對這些故事保持沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會造成深遠的後果 , 對於非暴力行為能夠成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有非常重要的共通點 , 兩者都是劇場的一種形式在尋找觀眾的理由 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一一個不斷收到頭版 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦議題 , 對非暴力領導人來說 , 變得非常困難 , 讓民間不服從者是可行的選項 , 來處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能不會讓房間裡的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓孩子拋下越來越大聲的手法是給予他第一次拋出符號的注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	幼兒時期的心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 自從小就知道 , 他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以激勵或激勵行為 , 單單透過給予孩子孩子的注意力 , 或加強他們的注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇關注的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東地區的衝突的核心 , 並將和平帶入非暴力行為的核心 , 是將非暴力行為轉變成一種功能性行為 , 做法是讓更多注意到現今在地面上非暴力領袖的注意力 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在把我的影片帶到西岸的村落、加薩和東耶路撒冷的村落中 , 我看到即使是一部紀錄片也能影響轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉杰的村落中 , 座落在耶路撒冷 , 這個社區面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 且沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們都在使用非暴力手段 , 但從來沒有人注意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一個篩選
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉辦了最好的節目 , 並且紀律地向約會展示 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯村的故事 , 被記錄在影片中 , 感覺到 , 的確有人在追隨他們在做什麼 , 有人在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列一邊 , 有一個新的和平運動叫做索里德里特 , 意指希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這個運動的領袖一直在用布德鲁斯村作為他們主要的招募工具之一
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報導以色列人以前從來沒有活躍過 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和固體運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小預算的獨立電影也可以扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力轉化成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大媒體玩家可以擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力示威 , 發生在村落中 , 像是畢爾本、尼林、瓦拉杰、耶路撒冷鄰里 , 如謝赫•賈拉和西爾瓦 , 非暴力的領導人會在他們的工作中變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解如果我們不去注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 就好像他們從未發生過那樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我第一手看到如果我們能做到 , 它們會加乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列的整體以色列巴勒斯坦衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力終於能夠解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證實了非暴力在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方工作
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓他們關注 , 讓他們可以證明它到處可行 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	simonsinek有一個簡單但強大的模式給予鼓舞人心的領導一切都從黃金圈開始 , 還有 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁•路德•金 , 和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 賣力 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大領袖如何激發行動
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要如何解釋當事情不如我們所假設的一樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的情況 , 如何解釋當其他人能夠實現那些看似會毀滅所有假設的事情時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦如此創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比所有他們的競爭對手更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有相同的才能、相同的機構、相同的顧問、相同的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導了民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受過普及權利折磨的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一的偉大演說者 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控權力的男子飛行 , 當肯定有其他隊伍更有資格、更有資金時......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現權力的男子飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我做了一項發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深改變了我對於世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我在裡面運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導者和組織 , 不論是蘋果電腦、馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟──他們都這麼認為、行動 , 並用同樣的方式溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是把它編碼出來 , 很可能是世界上最簡單的點子 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠啟發其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下術語 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值主張、你的專屬過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	談到 「 為什麼 」 , 我不是指 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	說到 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、溝通的方式 , 都來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的東西 , 到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導者和激勵人心的組織不管他們的體型 , 不管他們的產業全都認為、行動和從內而外溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦 , 因為他們很容易理解 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦跟其他人一樣 , 一個從他們的行銷訊息可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們很漂亮的設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友好 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」 「 嗯 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	大部分的行銷就是這樣 , 大部分的銷售都是這樣完成的 , 大部分的人際交流就是這樣 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們會說我們做的事 , 我們會說我們不同或我們如何比較好 , 我們會期待某種行為、購買、投票之類的 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師 , 擁有最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它能取得很好的汽油里程序 , 它有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	以下是蘋果電腦實際溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信去挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信不同的思考方式
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓產品有美好的設計 , 簡單的使用和使用者友好 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備要向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明 , 人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都能完美地買到蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒適 , 從蘋果電腦買mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區分它們的結構性和它們的競爭者不同 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出平面電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們多年來都在製作平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾夫和mp3球員和pdas一起出櫃 , 他們做出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 談到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從迪爾買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼要買電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標是不要和每個需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都建立在生物學的基礎上 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫切面 , 從上面往下看 , 你所看到的是人腦其實是分裂成三個主要元件 , 和黃金圈完美相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 會對應到 「 什麼 」 等級 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦新皮層負責所有的理性、分析的思想和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個部分構成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感覺 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、益處、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是無法驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們直接和大腦控制行為的部位交談 , 接著 , 我們允許人們用我們所說的有形的做法將它合理化 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給別人所有的事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節怎麼說 , 但感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用那個動詞 , 沒有 「 感覺 」 對不對 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的那部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們能提高的最好是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時候你說你帶著你的心 , 或者你帶著你的靈魂來領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭把它分解給你們 , 那些不是身體的其他部分在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的大腦邊緣區 , 控制決策而非語言的部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼要做你做的事 , 而人們會回應你為什麼要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓別人投票給你 , 或從你身上買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠 , 並想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你的東西的人 ; 目標是賣給相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這樣說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人只因為他們可以做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你相信的事的人 , 他們會用血汗和淚水為你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有其他比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人並不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 追求有權勢的人飛行就像是當天的點日com 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley擁有的 , 我們假設的 , 是成功的訣竅 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你相同的三個因素:低估、錯誤的人、市場狀況不佳的人 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三樣東西 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門給予五萬美元 , 來弄清楚這個飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉行了一個座位 , 在史密森尼時期工作 , 非常緊密 , 他知道當時所有的大心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心靈錢 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都在為langley紮根 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們為什麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley呢 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩遠 , 位在俄亥俄州、奧維爾和威爾堡萊特 , 他們完全沒有我們認為的成功的訣竅 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車商店的價格來支付他們的夢想 ; 在萊特兄弟的團隊中 , 沒有任何一個人接受大學教育 , 甚至不是歐維爾或威爾布爾 ; 而《紐約時報》卻無處不在 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同之處在於 , 歐維爾和威爾堡都是由一個目標所驅動 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能弄清楚這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人
and lo and behold , look what happened .	看 , 結果如何 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟的夢想與他們一起工作的人 , 帶著血汗、淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為支付費用 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說故事 , 每次萊特兄弟出去 , 他們就必須拿出五組零件 , 因為那是他們出去買餐前撞了多少次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟開始飛行 , 甚至沒有人在那裡體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley的動機是錯的:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個驚人的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的事物很重要呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某種東西叫做 「 創新的散播法則 」 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對知道它的術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數和喉頭 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一原因是你再也買不到輪級手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都待在不同時間點 , 在這規模的各個地方 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不可能有它 , 直到你達成了這15%到18%的市場滲透點 , 然後系統就會爆發 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你對新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約是10% 。 」 很驕傲地 ,
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過百分之十的客戶
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十的 「 取得它 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那感覺就像是: 「 喔 , 他們只是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到能得到的 , 而不是那些拿不到的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	就是這個 , 你必須關閉的這個小缺口 , 如同jeffreymoore稱之為 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的大多數人不會先嘗試某件事 , 直到其他人先嘗試它 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很自在地做出那些直覺的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更舒服地做那些直覺性的決定 , 由他們所相信的這個世界所驅動 , 而不僅僅是產品能取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人站在隊伍裡 , 花了六個小時買一支iphone , 當他們剛出櫃時 , 當你下週就可以走進店裡 , 買下架 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了4萬美金在平面電視上 , 剛出爐時 , 即使技術是次等的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想成為第一名
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做它 , 以及你做什麼 , 只要證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做證明他們相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們在頭六小時買iphone的原因是 , 排隊排隊六個小時 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看他們:他們是第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如前面所說 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的訣竅是金錢和對的人 , 以及對的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你當時應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	大約八、九年前 , 當今的今天 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下交易 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常高 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件太棒了 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我經常在垃圾時間華納dvr上綁著東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是商業的失敗
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股價大約是30或40美元 , 然後跌跌倒 , 從來沒有在10歲以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至在6歲以上交易除了幾次的小棘蛋糕以外
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品 , 可以暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 改寫現場電視節目 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 連你都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活的那種人 , 男孩 , 我們是否有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做它 , 而你所做的只是證明你相信什麼 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場聽金恩博士演講 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有發出任何邀請 , 也沒有網站來查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士並不是美國唯一一個很棒的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個受苦於公民權利的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很糟糕 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處走訪 , 告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們採取了他的成因 , 他們讓它成為了他們自己的 , 他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓更多人知道這個詞 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	看著 , 二十五萬人出現在對的時間 , 在對的時間聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為自己出櫃 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	正是他們對美國的信心 , 讓他們可以在公車上旅行八個小時 , 站在華盛頓的中央 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	那是他們相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:那些由更高權力所制定的法律和由人類所制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類制定的法律都與更高權威所制定的法律一致 , 我們將生活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	公民權利運動正是幫助他帶來生命的最佳因素 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 的演講 , 不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政治人物的話 , 用他們全面的12點計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們不鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和有領導者
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導的人卻激勵了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們都會跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人有能力激發他們周圍的人或找到激勵他們的人
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你把車停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝著正確的方向移動的 ? 神經科學家尼爾•布洛吉斯研究了我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在大型停車場 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並試著了解他大腦裡發生了什麼事
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 以黃色表示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那裡受損 , 就像阿茲海默症 , 你無法記住東西包括你把車停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是用拉丁文來命名為 「 海馬 」 , 它的名字很相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類的大腦裡有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元彼此溝通的方式是發送小脈衝或刺激通過彼此的連接
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成的 , 密度非常高 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 做法是從老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元記錄 , 或探索一個尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們將想像從這隻老鼠的海馬體中記錄下來的一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發電時 , 將會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以 , 我們看到的是 , 這種神經元知道每當老鼠在其環境中的某個特定位置 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送小型電波訊號到大腦的其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	這樣我們就可以將神經元的激發率顯示為動物的位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄下來 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入其環境中的不同部位時 , 不同的神經元會發射 , 比如 , 在這個正方形的箱子中 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們組成了一張圖 , 給大腦其他部分 , 持續地告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要大腦監控的電活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患在小鎮附近開車玩電玩遊戲 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	每當他們開車經過一個特定的地點時 , 就會開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個位置細胞怎麼知道老鼠或人在其環境中的哪個位置呢 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上頭的那隻喜歡在老鼠在盒子裡的牆壁中間射出 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你擴大箱子時 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的那一面 , 每當有一面牆靠近南邊時 , 都很喜歡開火 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放置另一面牆 , 細胞會在兩個地方開啟 , 不論在哪裡有一面牆 , 南邊都是動物在盒子裡探索的 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	這預測你周圍的界限與界線會延伸到建築物等等 , 對海馬體特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入值中 , 細胞會被發現 , 在海馬體中 , 海馬體的哪個專案計畫會完全反應 , 來偵測到邊界或邊緣 , 特別是從老鼠或老鼠的特定方向和方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物靠近牆壁或向東開界 , 不論是方形箱子的邊緣或圓形牆壁 , 或圓形箱子的圓形牆壁 , 或甚至桌子邊緣的一滴水滴水 , 都是動物跑來跑去的 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發射 , 每當南邊有限時 , 不論是桌子邊緣 , 或是牆壁 , 甚至兩張桌子間的隔閡都會被拉扯 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的位置 , 比如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境或你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變環境的因素 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗子在小方形環境中的位置 , 然後如果你問人們在哪裡 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟已經完全相同地伸展開來 , 位置細胞激發的位置 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	彷彿你記得旗幟的位置 , 藉由儲存位置細胞的圖案來儲存整個位置 , 然後你可以藉由移動到那個位置回到那個位置 , 以便你最好配合目前位置細胞的模式 , 配上儲存模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那引導你回到你想要記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過移動的位置 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把路徑放開 , 或許我們會停下來 , 我們就會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們就能整合這條路 , 大約是回頭的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一種叫做網格細胞的細胞中得到這種路徑整合輸入 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	同樣的 , 網格細胞在海馬體上的輸入 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每一組細胞都會在不同的位置射出 , 形成一個非常普通的三角網格 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個網格細胞的紀錄 , 這裡每個細胞都有類似網格的圖案在整個環境中 , 每個細胞的格狀網格會稍微變形 , 和其他的細胞有些相似 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這張圖上的紅色是綠色的 , 上面是藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 同心協力 , 老鼠可以在環境中放上發射的電網 , 有點像在地圖上找到的緯度和長距離線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 持續追蹤它的位置 , 讓它可以用它自己的動作來知道它的位置在它的環境中 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有類似網格的發射模式都有相同的對稱性 , 相同的網格的方向 , 在橘子上顯示 , 意味著所有網格細胞的網格活動 , 在大腦的某個特定區域 , 都應該改變 , 根據我們是否沿著六個方向跑 , 或沿六個方向跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進核磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像我剛剛給你們看的那個 , 並尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人類的腦內皮層也確實看到了 , 這和你在老鼠身上看到的網格細胞是一樣的 。
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他大概還記得他車子的位置 , 位置的距離和方向 , 將建築和界線延伸到他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞所呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從汽車公園裡取出的路徑 , 會在電網細胞發射中呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都能讓位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以回到他移動的位置 , 找到最好的位置 , 配合他大腦中儲存的位置細胞的發射模式 , 和他停車的地方 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個不敬視覺暗示的位置 , 像是他的車是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	或許已經被拖延了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去拿它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找類似這種網格的發射模式 , 我們在一系列的位置上看到它總是活躍的 , 當我們做各式各樣的自傳記憶任務時 , 例如記住上次參加婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 呈現我們周圍空間的神經機制也被用於產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們才能重現空間的景象 , 至少 , 在我們想想像的時候已經發生在我們身上的事件中 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	如果這正在發生 , 你的記憶可以從細胞互相啟動開始 , 通過這些密集的相互連結 , 然後重新啟動界線細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以在這個空間中移動這個視角點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種類型的細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們就像指南針一樣 , 根據你所面臨的情況 , 會開啟 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看方向 , 你想要為你的視覺圖像產生一個圖像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個婚禮上發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代在認知神經科學中的一個例子 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 例如你如何記住、想像 , 甚至思考 , 以數十億個神經元組成我們的大腦所做出的動作來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個全球安全驅動的動力 , 由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾的合作所驅動 。 這不僅僅是遠端期望開放式電扇 , 而是詹姆斯•史塔維迪斯 , 最高層的指揮官 , 最高層的太空總署 , 他們分享從近期的軍事歷史中生動的時刻 , 來解釋為何未來的安全 , 應該用橋樑而非牆壁來建造 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史塔維迪斯:nato的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會談到一點公開資源的安全性 , 因為我們必須在21世紀的安全上變得更好 。
